Incoming mail

Next Year's Plan for Railway Business and Joint Transportation (Continued)

Yu Yan, Director of the Business Department of the Ministry of Railways and Director of the Joint Transportation Office

(E) Increasing Transport Capacity - Railways must first have sufficient equipment to provide sufficient transport. Among the most important equipment, vehicles are the most important. Most of the roads in our country now feel that vehicles are in short supply. The fundamental reason is that vehicles are not sufficient in the first place, and there are many cases of vehicle inefficiency in operation, which makes the degree of shortage even more profound. In this situation, in order to enable the roads to have sufficient vehicles, on the one hand, we should try our best to use the existing vehicles to achieve their maximum effectiveness. On the other hand, we should also find ways to add new vehicles in order to fundamentally remedy the situation. Regarding the former, since taking office, I have followed the statistics of cargo ton-miles and freight car tonnage of the roads in 1919 and 1920 to show the degree of efficiency of vehicle use on the roads, so as to check the performance of vehicle use at any time. I am now engaged in formulating methods to improve vehicle distribution, which will be implemented in the coming year. In addition, we will take measures to shorten the loading, unloading, and transportation time of vehicles on the roads at any time, rush to repair damaged vehicles, and ban the detention of vehicles by the military, so as to increase the efficiency of vehicle turnover. Regarding the latter, the plan is roughly as follows: I have studied the methods of adding vehicles, which can be temporarily divided into four types: first, renting. This method can relieve the emergency for a while, but it is questionable whether vehicles can be rented at any time to meet the urgent needs. Second, self-manufacturing. This method is difficult to implement because railway machine factories mostly only have repair equipment. If the organization of machine factories is expanded to manufacture vehicles, it cannot be completed in a short period of time, nor can it be done with the current financial resources. Third, buying on credit. Conditions are agreed with the seller, and payment procedures are stipulated, and the purchased vehicles are used as collateral. Fourth, buying with cash. If cash can be raised, this method is the simplest and most direct. After careful consideration of the situation of the ministry and the roads, it is proposed to first use the last method. The ministry plans to raise funds to order vehicles for the roads, and after the vehicles arrive, they will be rented to the roads for use, and a corresponding rent will be collected to be used to repay the principal and interest of the vehicles. This matter is currently being planned. The above-mentioned opinions on increasing transport capacity are only in terms of vehicles. To increase transport capacity, it is naturally not limited to the issue of vehicles. Other equipment, such as how to add turnouts at each station and how to expand marshalling yards, to facilitate vehicle turnover, etc., will also be improved as far as possible.

(F) Improving Railway Freight Rates - Whether the freight rates set by a country's railways are appropriate affects not only its own business greatly, but also the price of goods, the stagnation of goods, the prosperity of the region, the civilization of the people, the prosperity and decline of various industries, and the quality of life of the people throughout the country, all of which are closely related. It goes without saying that it should be studied carefully and regulated carefully. At the beginning of the establishment of railways in our country, the right to set freight rates was controlled by foreigners. They were mostly isolated from the situation in our country and lacked research on the principles of freight rates. They arbitrarily set prices without standards, or even took the interests of foreign merchants as a prerequisite, ignoring the affordability of freight for domestic goods. The roads that were repaired later were not examined, and they were blindly copied, so that the movement of various goods was mostly inappropriate, either too high or unfair. There is a need for a complete reorganization. Moreover, since the implementation of responsible transportation, a 10% surcharge has been added to each freight rate. Whether the freight rate after the price increase is appropriate and what the impact is must also be reviewed and improved. Therefore, it is proposed to thoroughly reorganize the various factors that make up the approved freight rate: (1) The current freight grades are divided into six grades. It is proposed to study them in detail and appropriately increase them to ten grades. (2) The basic freight rates vary greatly from road to road. It is proposed to find ways to calculate the transportation costs of each road and then set them based on the transportation costs. (3) As far as possible, each road should try to use the method of gradual distance reduction, starting from roads with roughly equal mileage. (4) The proportion of freight rates between each grade varies from road to road, and even on the same route it is inconsistent. It is proposed to compare them with each other, study them in detail, and then reorganize them separately. (5) The proportion of the difference between the full car freight rate and the less-than-full car freight rate is 30% in some cases, 50% in some cases, and other proportions in some cases. It is proposed to conduct thorough research before reorganizing them. (6) The minimum weight of full car cargo. Our country's roads have no regulations to date, so the freight rates for loose and bulky goods are often difficult to calculate properly. We are now working on regulations for the minimum weight of various goods for various vehicles. Once the regulations are completed, they will be announced and implemented. Not only will the weight problem of loose and bulky goods be solved, but the proportion of the difference between the full car freight rate and the less-than-full car freight rate can also be used to make appropriate decisions. In short, the freight rates of railways in our country are mostly inappropriate and unfair. We must adhere to the spirit of developing railway business and revitalizing domestic industries as a fundamental reorganization plan. Although it is a major issue and may not be accomplished in a short period of time, we dare not fail to do our best to seek reorganization.

Spring and Autumn

A Commoner's Loving Mother

— Zhan Lu

The south eaves receive the sun, making winter warm. It is said that the winter sunlight is a yellow cotton coat or a natural stove, but these are only partial metaphors. To put it succinctly, it is simply a commoner's loving mother.

The warm room where commoners stop is, of course, the pleasure palace of the propertied class. If you are born with a bitter fate, you are only fit to run in the wind and snow and seek a living in the ice and frost. If you accidentally want to rest for a while in front of the door of the pleasure palace, you will either be scolded by the arrogant servant or barked loudly by the pretentious Pekingese dog. Fortunately, there are only snobbish people and snobbish dogs, but no snobbish sunlight. Wherever the thatched cottage and the sloping eaves are, where the bourgeoisie cannot reach, this commoner's loving mother will also come, embracing many poor people with frozen hands and feet, trembling all over, and giving them considerable comfort.

Every time the morning light is revealed, the blessed people who are sleeping soundly in the gold-decorated tents are reluctant to let the light in, because they do not need the dazzling sunlight. Only the poor people with runny noses, seeing the morning light, throw themselves into the embrace of nature's loving mother. Every ray of light is their lifeline. Even if they face the cold and do their hard work, under the protection of the loving mother, they can always reduce their pain. Suddenly, a patch of red clouds covered the face of the commoner's loving mother. The people in the gold-decorated tents happily got up to prepare invitations to open a banquet and enjoy the snow. Poor commoners, having lost the protection of their loving mother, had to spend another miserable cold night with runny noses.

I remember a great scholar who wrote about his childhood poverty, saying that in order to resist the bitter cold of the long night in the tattered quilt, he and his mother sat back to back, waiting for dawn. Only when the morning light broke through did they happily feel alive. It can be seen that even with the loving mother embracing them closely, the extremely poor people still cannot get rid of the cold. Only when this loving mother high in the clouds shows her face can there be hope of escaping death. Poets have always compared the loving mother to the spring sunshine, but it is not the spring sunshine. The commoner's loving mother is only this winter sunshine, which is as warm as embracing cotton.

A Review of Historical Materials on Diplomacy in the Late Qing Dynasty

— Da

There are three principles for studying the history of diplomacy in the late Qing Dynasty: first, credibility with evidence; second, detailed, substantial, and profound; and third, new documents. In general, the diplomacy of the Republic of China began in the late Qing Dynasty. Important documents at that time were not disclosed as a rule. Those who compiled historical books either relied on the writings of Chinese people or recorded the records of foreigners. It is a pity that it is not possible to get a glimpse of the whole picture from a few fragments. After reading the book "Historical Materials on Diplomacy in the Late Qing Dynasty" compiled by Mr. Wang Taofu and his son Wang Xiyin, I felt that it has made new contributions to these three principles. Here is a brief description:

First, according to the Qing system, princes led the Grand Council and concurrently managed the Zongli Yamen (Foreign Affairs Office). All important documents, even if they were not copied and distributed, were fully available to the Grand Council. The historical materials on diplomacy in the late Qing Dynasty were collected by Mr. Taofu when he worked in the Grand Council. The documents in this collection, regarding the process of establishing unequal treaties, consular jurisdiction, and the loss of tariff autonomy, as well as the meeting minutes of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and various envoys, are all collected without omission, which can be said to be credible and well-documented.

Second, diplomacy in the late Qing Dynasty was the most onerous. The details of various diplomatic issues such as the Yantai Treaty, the Tibet negotiations, the occupation of Myanmar, and the cases of Pianma, Hong Kong, Weihai, and Kowloon, etc.; the cases of Sino-American negotiations such as the protection of overseas Chinese, the General Arbitration Treaty, and the refund of indemnities, etc.; the cases of Sino-French negotiations such as the Franco-Vietnamese collusion, the Sino-French War, the border affairs of Guangdong, Yunnan, and Guangxi, and the Guangzhou Bay and Siming Guild Hall cases, etc.; the cases of Sino-Japanese negotiations such as the Sino-Japanese War, the cession of Ryukyu and Taiwan, the annexation of Japan and Korea, the return of Liaodong and Lushun, and the Shazipu, Nagasaki, Ershinmaru, Yanji, Dongsha Island, Luda Tianbaoshan logging, fishing, and the three northeastern provinces cases, etc.; the cases of Sino-German negotiations such as the dispatch of troops to Shandong and the leasing of Jiaozhou Bay, etc.; the cases of Sino-Russian negotiations such as the return of Yili, the leasing of Lushun, the Sino-Russian Secret Treaty, the Russo-Japanese War, the return of the three northeastern provinces, and the navigation of the Songhua and Heilongjiang rivers, etc.; and the cases of Sino-Italian negotiations such as the Sanmen Bay and Tianjin Yancha cases, etc., all of which are not available in ordinary history books, can be found in this compilation. It is very detailed, substantial, and profound.

Third, in this book, there are many new unpublished documents, such as the treaty agreed upon by the Zongli Yamen and Japan in the sixth year of Guangxu due to the Sino-Russian Yili issue; the correspondence files of the Sino-French negotiations on the Annam issue; Li Hongzhang and Weng Tonghe's memorials on peace and war when the Sino-Japanese War of Jiawu was about to break out; the documents on the private request of Li to go to Russia to make a secret treaty after the Sino-Japanese War; and the documents on Li's request to the court to take the blame for his actions when he went from Guangdong to Shanghai during the Boxer Rebellion. What is particularly valuable is the diplomatic history of the Xuantong Dynasty, which is extremely rare in today's publications. It can be said that all of them are documents that we have never seen before. Today, the loss of the four northeastern provinces is actually based on these documents. Here is a brief list of the major ones: the documents on the Sino-Japanese conference on various cases in the eastern provinces; the documents on the Sino-Korean border dispute cases; the correspondence files on Russia's invasion of the three northeastern provinces and the Xinjiang border; and the reports of envoys stationed abroad on the secret agreements between Russia and Japan. All of these have never been publicly announced in the past.

Men and Women

— Bin

Sister A'bao returned to Yang Village from Shanghai, dressed in gold and jade. At the age of twenty-nine, wouldn't she look as glamorous as a sixteen or seventeen-year-old girl in the eyes of the people of Yang Village?

Brother A'bing, seeing Sister A'bao's extravagance and liveliness, was very jealous and also set an auspicious day to go to Shanghai. Three years later, Brother A'bing returned, still a poorly dressed poor scholar!

Shanghai is the same Shanghai, and Yang Village is the same Yang Village, but Sister A'bao is a woman, and Brother A'bing is always a man!

Mixed-Blood Child

— Yang Yusheng

In several articles I have published in this journal, I seem to have frequently brought up the useless topic of how Chinese people are. Perhaps some may suspect that I am not Chinese.

On this point, I also feel very guilty. But after thinking it over, it seems that we cannot find a good impression on Chinese people. All Chinese people in the intellectual class can feel this. So, what can I say!

The reason why I keep harping on about Chinese people is that, although I dare not harbor the grand ambition of "criticizing the world," I am confident that my enthusiasm for "Chinese people to be good" is second to none! However, whether Chinese people can be good is another matter. It is a mistake to give up grumbling just because grumbling is ineffective!

As the editor of this journal said: "The hope of China lies in the general children of today." I have also found many opportunities to talk to them, but what they can give me is always somewhat "disappointing"! Especially "mixed-blood children" make me feel particularly sad!

I found a child of about seven or eight years old, born to a Chinese father and an American mother. He was very familiar with me and often brought the Blue Sky with a White Sun flag to my place to play. I pointed to the small flag in his hand and asked him in English—because he couldn't speak Mandarin—"What is this?" He replied, "This is a national flag."

I said, "Is this the flag of the United States?" The answer was: "No, this is not 'our' flag, this is 'your' Chinese flag!"

Ah! Think about it, the terms "you" and "we" were already deeply imprinted in his mind! This little thing!

I asked him again: "Your father desperately teaches you to write Chinese characters, speak Chinese, and read Chinese books. Aren't you a Chinese? Do you want to be a Chinese?" He replied, "No, I want to be Japanese!" I asked him why? He said Japanese planes are more powerful than Chinese planes. At the same time, he made gestures, pursed his little mouth, and rhythmically shouted "Ooh... bang... bang..." as if instructing me on the situation of the bombs falling!

Of course, it's no wonder I got angry. I shouted loudly, "Shut up!" Before the next sentence, "Get out," could be uttered, he had already slipped away!

Since then, he has not dared to meet me. On this point, I feel very happy!

Northeast Fourth Company Commander

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 21: Whispered Advice Under the Lamp, Exhorting the Weakling, Coldly Watching Heroes From The Foot of the Mountain

In the past, Gui Zhi would always retort every sentence her mother said. But today, for some unknown reason, her mother's words seemed to have a deeper meaning, and she dared not say much, lowered her head, and walked into her bedroom. The more she was like this, the more suspicious Madam Jiang became. She sat in the room for a while, pushed open the door, and looked at the sky, muttering to herself: "Oh! In a little while, the dark clouds are all over the sky. It may rain again tonight. I'll go outside to check the weather. It's better if it doesn't rain, because I still need to take apart the quilts and wash them tomorrow." As she said this, she walked out. Outside the gate, two children from the neighborhood were still playing by the road. Just as she was about to inquire, one of the children came up and asked: "Madam Yang, did your eldest daughter find the key she lost?" Madam Jiang said, "How do you know she lost her key?" The child pointed to the ground in front of him and said: "Eldest Daughter Yang was dazed there for a long time, looking for it for a long time." Madam Jiang said: "She doesn't usually walk that way, how could she have gone there?" The child said: "Are you saying I'm accusing you wrongly? If you don't believe me, go back and ask Grandpa Gan San, and you'll know. He was standing there, talking to Grandpa Gan Er for a long time." When Madam Jiang heard this, she couldn't help but feel a cold sweat from every pore on her body. She glared at the child and said: "I told him to collect old debts from Grandpa Gan Er. What could they have to say?" She explained to Gui Zhi in this way, but her heart was pounding, thinking that Gui Zhi, this child, was indeed acting strangely lately. Just seeing her hide a photo of Grandpa Gan Er under her pillow when she sleeps, she knew that her talk with Grandpa Gan Er was not an ordinary appointment. She kept this matter in her heart and felt uneasy. In the evening, Gui Zhi, whether she was deliberately pretending to be calm or extremely bored, took a few small newspapers and read them by the lamp. Madam Jiang also held a newly cut piece of fabric and sewed a short coat under the lamp. The mother and daughter sat together, sharing one corner of the table. (280)

*Unintelligible text*

Recollections of a Trip to Min (Part 1)

A few months ago, I had the opportunity to visit Fuzhou, the capital of Fujian Province, twice. Traveling across the vast ocean was a first for me in my life. Such a grand tour should be recorded, but I, being a lazy person, find it very difficult to pick up a pen and write. Therefore, I procrastinated for a long time and didn't write a single word. Recently, I saw in the newspaper that the Fujian under the rule of the 19th Route Army is in turmoil again. Only three months have passed, but the situation is hazy. Writing down these random thoughts can be considered as leaving a trace of my experiences.

Fuzhou is located in the southern part of our country. From Shanghai, it takes about forty-seven or forty-eight hours by boat to reach. According to experienced sailors: "The waves in the South Seas are soft, while the waves in this ocean are hard. Hard waves are easier to bear, while soft waves are difficult to endure." Therefore, the waves on the way to Fuzhou are very difficult to bear. However, being stubborn by nature, I don't buy into anything easily. I thought that in the Huangpu River in Shanghai, I had been on small sampans with raging winds and waves, and had never been seasick. How could I get seasick in a ship with a wider area? Little did I know that by the time we left the Wusongkou and reached the waters of Ningbo, my head was already unstable. Later, I couldn't even sit, and couldn't eat. I only ate some porridge. This sea journey was like spending a few days sick. It wasn't until the ship was approaching the Mawei that the ship became stable, and my heart felt like waking up after being drunk, and I slowly felt refreshed.

Mawei is a strategic point of Fuzhou, also known as Mawei, and also has the names of Madu River and Matou River. That place has overlapping mountains and deep harbor waters that can accommodate large ships. After the ship enters the port, it twists and turns. All around are mountains. When the mountains end, a turn reveals green waves and overlapping green hills, which is a whole new world. "When the mountains and rivers are exhausted, one doubts there is no road ahead, but a village appears with willows and flowers in bloom." This kind of realm is truly indescribably pleasant. Mawei is one of the reasons why Fuzhou haunts my dreams. However, I went to Fuzhou twice and passed through Mawei four times. Every time I passed through, listening to the weeping water, my heart was always unhappy, because Mawei fifty years ago, around the tenth year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, the French fleet harassed Fujian, and the Battle of Mawei was the most heartbreaking page in our country's history of shame. So every time I passed through, I couldn't help but sigh and pay tribute. I remember I once had two lines of poetry: "The flowing water should know the hatred of the fallen country, and the raging waves roar like the voice of a great lion." I wrote this while on the way to Mawei.

The terrain of Mawei is indeed very dangerous, so it is also one of the important military ports of our country. There are shipyards, docks, naval hospitals, naval schools, etc. there. Unfortunately, the ship passed by in a flash, and I didn't have the opportunity to visit them one by one.

After the ship anchored in Mawei, many people jumped up and asked if anyone wanted to hire a "kailongyang". At first, I was confused, but later I learned that "kailongyang" is a small gasoline boat, probably about seven or eight yuan per boat, and it takes about two hours to reach Nantai outside Fuzhou city.

Nantai was a trading port opened up during the Opium War when five ports were opened for trade, so it is the most lively place outside the city. The YMCA is also here, as well as many brothels and large hotels. The market is very prosperous. In front of Nantai is the Min River, with flowing water, never stopping day and night. There is a small island in the river, with a large bridge connecting the two. The south bridge is called Jiangnan, and the north bridge is called Wanshou, totaling 140 zhang in length. The engineering is very grand. The water under the bridge is very turbulent, especially when the tide rises, it is even more surging and powerful, like a thousand troops and ten thousand horses.

The streets of Fuzhou are well-built, the roads are also wide, and the municipal administration is pretty good. However, the rickshaws there are not well-constructed, and it is not comfortable to sit on. Fuzhou has a special kind of banyan tree. This kind of tree grows branches on the trunk, and roots grow out of the branches, hanging down to the ground, and then becoming trunks again. Therefore, its shade is very large. Its leaves are round and smooth. We can see them everywhere on the road. In summer, the dense shade blocks the sun and attracts wind. Banyan trees are very useful. Speaking of its origin, it is found in both Fujian and Guangdong, but Fuzhou is especially famous. So Fuzhou also has another name, called Banyan City. This is what my friend Mr. W told me.

Page 12

Education News from Other Provinces

Second Annual Meeting of the Chinese Testing Society

Held in Beijing Today

The second annual meeting of the Chinese Testing Society is scheduled to be held in the Zhizhi Hall of the Central University in the capital at 9:00 AM today. The history of the society, recent research work, and papers of this session are recorded separately as follows:

Brief History In the autumn of the 19th year, Dai Jitao, the president of the Examination Yuan, believed that the examination system was established by the late Dr. Sun Yat-sen and that testing was a method of the examination system. Therefore, he had the intention to initiate the organization of this society. At that time, the Central Party Headquarters had a testing section, which was headed by Mr. Wu Nanxuan. Mr. Wu, together with Mr. Shi Weihuan and Mr. Lai Lian, began preliminary preparations. The staff of the testing section drafted the organization and work plan, and a draft of the regulations. The first draft was completed on October 14, and initiators were solicited. By December 15, a total of 57 people agreed. According to the law, a statement of reasons was prepared and submitted to the Nanjing Special City Party Headquarters for permission to organize. On January 20 of the 20th year, permission to organize was granted and a permit was issued. Subsequently, a communication election was held using the named joint and several voting method. As a result, Wu Nanxuan, Ai Wei, Yi Kechun, Chen Heqin, Shi Weihuan, Gu Kebin, Zhuang Zexuan, Liao Maoru, and Yu Shuangqiu were elected as preparatory members. Chen Xuan, Shan Lu Zhiwei, Guo Yicen, Wang Shulin, and Peng Baichuan were elected as alternate preparatory members. Wu Nanxuan was designated to be responsible for convening preparatory meetings, establishing a preparatory committee, and electing Wu Nanxuan, Peng Baichuan, and Yi Kechun as executive committee members. Membership was also solicited. By June 21, the inaugural meeting and the first member meeting were held in the Zhizhi Hall of the Central University. The articles of association and work plan were approved, and Ai Wei, Yi Kechun, Heqin Gu Kebin, Peng Baichuan, Liao Shicheng, and Shi Weihuan were elected as directors. Wu Nanxuan, Wang Shulin, and Lu Zhiwei were elected as alternate directors. On July 17 of the 21st year, the first annual meeting was held at Yenching University in Beijing, lasting four days. A total of eleven papers were read, all of which were the results of the members' daily research. In August, the second board of directors was established, and No. 13 Langbei Street, Nanjing was rented as the address of the society. The members worked very hard at this time and did not slacken due to financial difficulties during the national crisis. Many books and instruments were also purchased at this time. This annual meeting was originally scheduled to be held during the summer of this year, but due to insufficient preparation, it was postponed to the present time. Prior to the meeting, the board of directors elected seven members of the annual meeting preparation committee, divided into four committees for papers, reception, document affairs, and separately prepared. Dai Jitao was appointed as honorary director, and Xiao Xiaorong and Wu Nanxuan were appointed as director and deputy director, respectively. Liu Naijing, Tong Runzhi, Huang Longxian, and Yi Kechun were responsible for the affairs of each committee. The preparation committee held four meetings. This is a rough outline of the evolution of the society since its establishment.

Research Work The research work of this society is undertaken by each member independently. For research problems that are too large, the association will provide research subsidies. The results are either published in the association's magazine ("Testing") or printed into separate publications. The testing magazine has now been published to the fourth issue, and seven separate research reports have been published. In addition, a series of books and special publications are being compiled, and one book is currently being printed. The following is a list of the members' research that has been reported: (1) Chinese National Language Testing This research is led by Mr. Ai Wei and has been in progress for five years. (2) English Testing for Freshmen in College, also led by Mr. Ai Wei. (3) Investigation of Unlimited Association of Chinese Children, led by Mr. Lu Zhiwei. (4) Preliminary Study of the Development of Memory Forms, undertaken by Mr. Xiao Xiaorong, with a separate publication. (5) Three Major Problems of Intelligence Testing, also led by Mr. Xiao Xiaorong, also with a separate publication. (6) Comparative Study of Ethical Concepts between Two Ethnic Groups, led by Mr. Zhang Yi. (7) Experiment on the Teaching Methods of Two Decimal Multiplication Methods, led by Mr. Zhou Xuezhang. (8) Comparative Study of the Speed of Horizontal and Vertical Writing of Chinese Characters, led by Mr. Cai Lesheng. (9) Initial Trial Use of T.B.C.F. System in France, undertaken by Mr. Zuo Chengsi. (10) Multifaceted Adaptive Intelligence Testing, led by Mr. Xiao Xiaorong. (11) Revised Bina-Simon Intelligence Testing, undertaken separately by Lu Zhiwei and Wu Tianmin. (12) Composition Scale, compiled by Mr. Zhou Xuezhang. (13) Research on Four Kinds of Hand Movements, led by Mr. Xiao Xiaorong, with a separate publication. (14) Research on the Ability of Eye-Hand Coordination, also undertaken by Mr. Xiao Xiaorong, and also with a separate publication. (15) Explanation of Thorndike's Law of Effect, also undertaken by Mr. Xiao Xiaorong, also with a separate publication. (16) Relationship between Calligraphy Progress and Practice Time, undertaken separately by Mr. Zeng Renqian and Mr. Shen Guanqun, also with a separate publication. (17) Revised Intelligence Testing for Young Children, led by Mr. Xiao Xiaorong. (18) Research on Hand Movements, undertaken by Mr. Xiao Xiaorong, with a separate publication. (19) Research on Curve Fitting, undertaken by Mr. Ai Wei. (20) Two-Factor Theory, undertaken by Mr. Wang Shulin. (21) Theory, Practice, and Promotion of Educational Diagnosis, undertaken by Mr. Du Yuanzai.

Future Plans The association's plans for the coming year are divided into four categories: (1) Pilot Police Testing; (2) Analysis of Basic Teaching Materials; (3) High School Student Graduation Examination System; (4) Elementary School Student Graduation Examination System; (5) Evaluation of Essay-Style Examination Papers by Three Parties; (6) Relationship between the Number of Essay-Style Examination Questions and Reliability; (7) Clarification of Testing and Statistical Terms; (8) Compilation of Elementary School Natural Science Testing; (9) Compilation of Elementary School Social Science Testing; (10) Compilation of Elementary School Arithmetic Testing; (11) Compilation of Junior High School Biology Testing; (12) Compilation of High School Biology Testing; (13) Compilation of Adult Graphic Intelligence Testing; (14) Compilation of Literacy Language Testing for Popular Schools; (2) Compilation, Translation, and Publication Matters: (1) Testing Four Issues; (2) Book Series Five Types; (3) Research Special Publication Fourteen Types; (4) Research Report Twenty Types; (3) General Affairs: (1) Collection of Books and Newspapers; (2) Fundraising; (3) Fundraising; (4) Promotion Matters: Hold Ten Public Lectures.

Annual Meeting Papers The current annual meeting papers have collected and measured eighteen papers, all of which are members' research experience, which are described as follows: 1. Testing Work of Dingxian Pingjiao Association, Zhou Xiangeng, Zhuge Long, 2. Testing on the Color Preferences of Chinese Students, Zhou Xiangeng, Chen Hanbiao, Comparison of Abnormal Tendencies of French, American and Chinese University Students, Zhou Xiangeng, Zhu Jingyuan, 4. Analysis of American Judgment of Chinese Characters Upside Down, Zhou Xiangeng, Lei Zhaotang, 5. University Entrance Examination and Intelligence Testing, Shen Yougan, 6. Comparison of Chinese Character Horizontal and Vertical Writing Connectivity, (2) Cai Lesheng, 7. Non-text Intelligence Testing for Adults, Chen Lijiang, 8. New Test Paper Made by National Central University Experimental School, Xi Qichang, 19. Preliminary Research Plan on the Judgment Method of Commenting on Essay-style Test Papers, Yi Kechun,

Staff Members Current staff members of the association, Directors Ai Wei, Chen Heqin, Yi Kechun, Lu Zhiwei, Wang Shulin, Huang Longxian, Liao Shicheng, Alternate Directors Peng Baichuan, Xiao Xiaorong, Gu Kebin, members of the Translation Committee Xiao Xiaorong, Wang Shulin, Liu Naijing, Wu Nanxuan, Peng Baichuan (above are standing committee members) Lu Zhiwei, Zhou Xuezhang, Liu Tingfang, Chen Heqin, Liao Shicheng, Shen Yougan, Chen Xuan, Shan Yu Ziyi, Huang Yi, Zhang Yaoxiang, Gu Kebin, Ai Wei, Pan Shu, Xiao Chengzhen, Shi Meixuan, Yi Kechun, Li Qing Song, Ma Futan, Tong Runzhi, Xia Chengfeng, Director of Research Department Xiao Xiaorong, Director of Affairs Department Yi Kechun, Resident Ping Secretary Lu Zhiwei, Resident Shanghai Secretary Chen Heqin, There are a total of 174 members, including 51 university professors, 37 middle school faculty members, 27 elementary school faculty members, 25 civil servants, 14 party affairs workers, 18 university students, 1 foreign member, and 1 group.

Amidst Calls for Independent Education Funding, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Jiangxi, Henan, and Fujian Provinces Have Achieved Education Funding Independence

But the government has no such proposition, making it even more difficult to raise funds

The twelve education personnel dispatched by the Ministry of Education to inspect various provinces and cities have returned to the Ministry one after another. Detailed reports on the inspections are being compiled separately by each member and will not be released within the year. We have interviewed various members to gather information on the total education funding and the status of education funding independence in the provinces and cities they visited (a total of twenty provinces and cities), which is recorded below:

(1) Jiangsu Province's education funding is completely independent, with the establishment of the Jiangsu Education Funding Management Office, which directly collects special education funds from various counties in Jiangsu. The actual expenditure for the current year for various provinces, schools, and provincial education institutions is approximately four million yuan per month, of which 3.8 million yuan comes from land tax and slaughter and tooth tax, and 200,000 yuan from school administrative income. (The budget originally listed 4.3 million yuan, but in reality, the item of school administrative income was canceled due to the provincial order not to collect tuition and accommodation fees, and the subsidy of 300,000 yuan from the finance department has not been paid in recent years. This year, due to the cancellation of tuition and accommodation fees, the finance department allocated two jiao per shi of transported grain collected to education, which translates to an actual revenue of approximately 200,000 yuan to offset the tuition and accommodation fees. Therefore, the so-called subsidy of 300,000 yuan from the finance department is even more difficult to pay, so only 4 million yuan is available.)

(2) Zhejiang Province's education funding has recently become independent. The provincial government has resolved to implement the special education funds and payment methods for Zhejiang Province. The total education funding for Zhejiang Province is over 2.106 million yuan, of which 1.2 million yuan comes from foil business tax, 200,000 yuan from tobacco and alcohol surtax, and 600,000 yuan from slaughter business tax.

(3) Nanjing City's education funding is in the planning and preparation stage for independence. The total education funding for the city (including various city schools and municipal education institutions under the social affairs bureau) is 600,000 yuan.

(4) Shanghai City's education funding is not yet independent. The total education funding for the city is over 1.22 million yuan.

(5) Anhui Province's education funding is not yet independent. The total education funding for the province is over 2.6 million yuan, of which 1.2 million yuan is subsidized by the central government, and the remainder is provided by the provincial treasury.

(6) Jiangxi Province's education funding is already independent, with a management committee overseeing its use. The Education Funding Management Office distributes the salt surtax received from the West Bank Tax Collection Bureau to various schools and provincial education institutions on a monthly basis. The total education funding for the province is 2 million yuan.

(7) Hunan Province is in the process of seeking education funding independence. According to Director Zhang of the provincial finance department in a conversation with Section Chief Wu of the Ministry of Education, 80,000 yuan can be allocated monthly starting from the next semester, and education funding can be independent. The total education funding for the province is 1.92 million yuan, with 108,000 yuan per month from the central salt surtax, and the remaining 52,000 yuan provided by the provincial treasury. The central government subsidy is not in arrears, but the provincial funds are currently received at 70% of the full amount, and it is feared that it will be 60% in the next semester. Therefore, education in Hunan Province is currently facing difficulties.

(8) Hubei Province is in the process of seeking education funding independence. The total education funding for the province is 2.4 million yuan.

(9) Guangdong Province's education funding does not have any problems in terms of the system, so there is no need for independence. The estimated education funding for the province is 3,210,821 yuan (excluding local education funding).

(10) Guangxi Province's education funding has never been in arrears and does not seek independence. The education funding for the province is 3,434,680 yuan (including local education funding).

(11) Henan Province's education funding is already independent, with the establishment of an Education Funding and Property Management Office. The education funding for the province is 2,375,192 yuan.

(12) Shaanxi Province's education funding is not yet independent in terms of revenue sources, with only a management office responsible for payment. The education funding for the province is 921,378 yuan.

(13) Fujian Province's education funding, according to the Ministry of Education inspector who returned from inspection last month, is already independent, with the establishment of an Education Funding Management Committee. The education funding for the province is 1,633,368 yuan, of which the central government allocates 110,000 yuan per month from the salt tax, and the remainder is provided by the provincial treasury. In addition, the local education funding belonging to various counties totals over 1.71 million yuan.

(14) Shanxi Province's education funding is not easy to become independent. The education funding for the province is over 1.9 million yuan.

(15) Suiyuan's education funding is also not easy to become independent, amounting to 280,000 yuan.

(16) Chahar's education funding is also difficult to become independent, amounting to 240,000 yuan.

(17) Shandong Province's education funding is not yet independent. The education funding for the province is 3,031,399 yuan, and the local education funding is 4,365,143 yuan.

(18) Qingdao City's education funding is not yet independent. The education funding for the city is approximately 530,000 yuan. (The reporter interviewed the current inspectors within half an hour, so the record for this city is approximate due to inaccurate information.)

(19) Hebei Province's education funding is not yet independent. The education funding for the province is 3.4 million yuan.

(20) Beiping City's education funding is not yet independent. The total education funding for the city is 960,000 yuan per year, or 80,000 yuan per month, of which 25,000 yuan per month is from the central government subsidy.

The Government's Attitude Towards Independent Education Funding: According to the Riri News Agency, since the outbreak of the September 18th Incident, due to the empty national treasury, the education funding of various provinces and cities has become even more strained, resulting in salary arrears for several months. In order to promote education administration and strive to rectify funding, the education authorities of various provinces and cities have generally advocated for independent funding. The Riri News Agency's Beijing correspondent specifically inquired about this matter with the person in charge of the Ministry of Education, who stated that since the 16th year of the Republic of China (1927), the country has been in continuous warfare, and the people are impoverished, resulting in the failure to allocate education funding on schedule, which is regrettable. Now, the provinces' request for independent funding seems justified, but implementation must have a corresponding income as fixed funding, otherwise it will still be a pie in the sky. Even collecting national taxes to cover national military and political expenses is not enough to make up for even a fraction of the needs, let alone allocating funds as fixed education funding. As for the education funding of Jiangsu and Fujian provinces, it was originally independent. Except for Fujian Province, which ultimately failed due to a certain matter, Jiangsu Province originally had the establishment of the Jiangsu Education Funding Management Committee, but recently the funds have also been misappropriated, resulting in arrears. Currently, all national universities, except for Tsinghua University, which has the Sino-American Boxer Indemnity as a foundation, are not independent. If they want to achieve it, the government still has no reserve funds. Considering the current difficulties, the Ministry believes that before education funding becomes independent, it should strive for the average allocation of all education funding.

Shanghai's Independence Movement: The Shanghai Municipal Secondary School Teachers' Union held its ninth regular meeting yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM. All executive directors were present, with Chen Jicheng as the chairman and Xu Xingchu as the recorder. The following key matters were resolved: (1) The time for the New Year's member get-together was changed to 11:00 AM to 2:00 PM, and the location remained at the YMCA in Baxianqiao. The resolution was passed. (2) A request was made to invite Director Pan to give a speech. The resolution was passed. (3) How should entertainment programs be stipulated? The following resolutions were made: 1. Individualized exchange performances, 2. Raffle gifts (each person can get at least two or more candies, books, stationery, etc.), 3. Member solos, 4. Relocation of the union's office. It was resolved to move to the second floor of the Shanghai Bank in Ximen. 5. Letters were sent to various bookstores requesting secondary school textbooks for various subjects to facilitate research and introduction. The resolution was passed. 6. A survey was conducted with the academic affairs offices of various secondary schools to investigate the textbook names, publication locations, and authors used in various subjects. The resolution was passed. 7. A petition was submitted to the Ministry of Education and the Education Bureau to unify social science textbooks to facilitate teaching. The resolution was passed. 8. The establishment of a secondary school library. The resolution was passed and handed over to the research department for design. 9. A movement was launched for independent education funding in Shanghai. It was resolved to petition the Ministry of Education and the Municipal Government to designate reliable tax revenue in the city as the city's education funding, with the amount accounting for at least one-quarter of the city's funding, and to designate an independent institution to be responsible for handling it. The meeting adjourned after the resolutions were made.

Ministry of Education Approves Exam Dates for Middle Schools in the Capital

January 15th to 17th

The Ministry of Education, based on the Nanjing Municipal Social Affairs Bureau's report clarifying the measures for the upper semester graduation examinations for middle school students in the city in the 22nd year of the Republic of China (1933), made appropriate changes based on the Ministry's regulations and requested that points not yet stipulated be recorded and requested clarification of Article 10 of the regulations regarding the number of times a student can repeat a grade. Yesterday, the Ministry of Education instructed the bureau to explain each article as follows: (1) The city's middle school entrance examinations are approved to be postponed to January 15th to 17th. (2) The section on recruiting new students with the same academic ability as junior high school graduates in senior high school entrance examinations has already been clearly stipulated by the Ministry in the middle school regulations. Therefore, no additional regulations have been added in the entrance examination regulations. The bureau may issue certificates for students who fail one or two subjects in the junior high school entrance examinations to apply for further education. (3) The entrance examination pass certificate is originally intended for students to apply for further education. If the schools under the bureau can issue the graduated certificates that have been verified according to the time stipulated in Article 11 of the entrance examination regulations, the bureau does not need to issue this certificate separately. (4) Junior high school graduates who take vocational subjects in the entrance examination do not need to take foreign languages again. (5) Students who failed the natural science subject in the previous junior high school entrance examination should be allowed to retake the two subjects of physics, chemistry, and biology. Those who failed history or geography should be allowed to retake the failed part of the history and geography subject. (6) If a student cannot participate in the entrance examination due to illness or other reasons and requests a makeup exam afterwards, it should be decided by the city's Middle School Student Graduation Entrance Examination Committee whether to allow the makeup exam or only allow the makeup exam in the next entrance examination. (7) Article 64 of the Middle School Regulations states that "repeating a grade is limited to once," which refers to repeating a grade for one academic year. However, since many middle schools in various provinces and cities have classes that start in the spring, it is necessary to hold two entrance examinations. Students who fail three subjects in the entrance examination and repeat a grade can participate in the entrance examination twice. These students are nominally repeating a grade twice, but in fact, they are only repeating a grade for one academic year. The provisions of Article 10 of the entrance examination regulations are not inconsistent with the provisions of Article 64 of the Middle School Regulations. You should be informed of this. This order.

The Ministry of Education Cracks Down on Government-Funded Students Who Have Returned Home

(Central News Agency, Nanjing, 28th) The Ministry of Education has learned that among the government-funded students or subsidized students in various provinces, some have completed their studies or have not completed their studies, and have already returned home, but are still receiving money from the Education Bureau on a monthly basis. It has ordered the various Education Bureaus to strictly crack down on this.

Local News

The Ministry of Education Orders Shanghai Universities to Allow Fujian Students to Audit Temporarily

Yesterday, the Ministry of Education ordered six public and private universities in Shanghai, stating, "We have repeatedly received petitions from students from various private universities or colleges in Fujian Province, stating that they have left school and come to Beijing due to the Fujian Incident, and requesting designated schools for transfer or auditing, etc. After investigation, these students have special circumstances, so we should consider ways to help them. If your school has surplus capacity, students holding certificates such as payment receipts or lecture certificates, etc., and have been verified by the school as genuine, can be allowed to audit temporarily in corresponding classes. In addition to issuing separate orders, this order is issued for your school to comply with."

The Affiliated Middle School of Jinan University Has Returned to Normal

The two directors of education and training are temporarily replaced by Yuan Yeyu and Tang Tonghou

Yesterday, the senior high school continued to have classes, and the junior high school Boy Scouts held an inspection and camping event

According to Shanghai News, the students of the Affiliated Middle School of National Jinan University were dissatisfied with the director of the affiliated middle school, Kuang Songling, which led to a wave of expulsions of faculty and staff. The details have been reported in previous news. Yesterday, the school order was as usual, and the students attended classes with peace of mind. The junior high school Boy Scouts held an inspection and camping event. The details are recorded separately as follows:

School Situation: Yesterday, the entire affiliated middle school had returned to normal, and the students attended classes with peace of mind. Director Kuang did not come to school, and his duties were temporarily assumed by Principal Zheng. Dean of Academic Affairs Zhang Daoshen and Dean of Student Affairs Guan Kebui have also left the school. All Dean of Academic Affairs duties are temporarily assumed by teacher Yuan Yeyu, and the Student Affairs Director duties are temporarily assumed by full-time teacher Tang Tonghou. Most of the faculty and staff have returned to school to perform their duties.

Student Statement: Student representative He Guozhang of the school told the Shanghai News reporter yesterday, "The turmoil in our school this time was purely due to Director Kuang's lack of teaching and management skills. Since taking office, he has forced more than 100 overseas Chinese students to leave the school. The students have expressed their dissatisfaction, which has been brewing until now, leading to the outbreak. Now that Director Kuang has left, there should be no other problems. We are still attending classes as usual every day."

Boy Scout Inspection: Yesterday was the sixth anniversary of the establishment of the 64th Boy Scout Troop of the junior high school department. At the same time, the Rover Scouts and Boy Scouts of the university and senior high school departments resumed their activities. An inspection was held in the morning, and camping was held near the school in the afternoon. A bonfire was held in the evening, which was entirely organized by the students themselves. The order was quite good.

Statement from the Shanghai Alumni Association of Jinan University: Since the turmoil occurred in the Affiliated Middle School of National Jinan University, the Shanghai Alumni Association of Jinan University has repeatedly convened joint meetings of executive and supervisory committee members, and unanimously resolved to safeguard the alma mater, support Principal Zheng, and telegraph the Central Party Headquarters, the Ministry of Education, and the school's trustees, etc., to quickly order the situation to be stopped in order to quell the turmoil. Although the turmoil in the affiliated middle school has eased, the association is still concerned that the students of the affiliated middle school may be used by others to create further incidents, so it has organized a special committee to deal with all contingencies. The association's express mail telegram to the Central Party Headquarters, the Ministry of Education, and the school's trustees, etc., is recorded as follows: (Omitted above) Extremely Urgent. Students in the middle school department of Jinan University suddenly went on strike at 9:00 AM on the 20th of this month (December), although it was very brief and classes were resumed immediately. However, the actions of the students in the middle school department were kept secret beforehand and strictly silent afterwards. Only at 9:00 AM on the morning of this day did a portion of the students in the middle school department order the faculty and staff of the middle school office to cease operations and teaching. At that time, because the incident happened suddenly, the school authorities were unable to stop it until 7:00 PM when the students automatically attended self-study classes. This morning, they arrived on time for classes and lectures. The course of events, from the outside, seems very mild and has come to an end. But in reality, it is not. According to a thorough investigation after the adjournment, the students in the middle school department have excessive demands on the school authorities. If this is the case, then although classes have resumed in name, it will be extremely difficult to deal with the aftermath. Currently, Principal Zheng can only concurrently serve as the director of the department to maintain the situation before Director Kuang returns to the school. However, at this time of instability and rumors, it is appropriate to use the sound of reading to capture the floating of society. My colleagues are deeply concerned about the current situation and are especially unwilling for more incidents to occur as the semester is about to end. Therefore, we earnestly request that your department (your leader) take appropriate measures to quickly deal with the situation and strictly order the students in the middle school department to restore the school's normal state, concentrate on their studies, and not make any further demands. If the school spirit is not rectified from the root, the victims will not only be Jinan University alone, and I am afraid that the students of various schools in Shanghai will unfortunately be drawn into the vortex and used by conspirators, and the impact is unimaginable. I am terrified and unable to express my expectations for orders and instructions. Respectfully, the Shanghai Alumni Association of National Jinan University.

Sports

Jinan University Wins Soccer Championship, Retaining the Title

Ties Fudan 1-1 Yesterday

—An Exceptionally Polite Game—

The Jiangnan University Sports Association Soccer Championship concluded yesterday, with Jinan University continuing its hegemony. Yesterday's match against Fudan was held at the China Baseball Field. Both sides played exceptionally politely, resulting in a 1-1 draw. A truly harmonious result.

No Scores in the First Half: But because of excessive politeness, the situation turned dull. In the first half, both sides went back and forth without scoring. If there were no opportunities, they would never force the ball when it reached the goal. It seemed that both sides had an agreement in advance not to infringe on each other. If all soccer games could be like this, then emotions would naturally be harmonious, and disputes would disappear.

Each Side Scores a Goal in the Second Half: About a quarter of an hour into the second half, Luo Haiguang of Jinan University scored a goal against Fudan, but in less than three minutes, Lu Xiuwen of Fudan returned a goal, resulting in a 1-1 draw. Jinan University thus won the championship with a record of five wins and one draw. The lineup and results of each team are as follows:

Shen Huichun Incident of Being Beaten Up Has Been Entrusted to a Lawyer for Litigation

To Uphold the Law and Manifest Human Rights

To Serve as a Warning to Others and Prevent Future Problems

Jiangnan University Suspends Jiaotong University from Competition for One Year

The Shanghai China Sports Referees Association held a temporary meeting on the 25th at Taihe Enclosure to discuss how to deal with the case of its member Shen Huichun being beaten by Jiaotong University students at the Jiaotong University stadium while officiating the Jiangnan University vs. Jiaotong University soccer game. At the same time, the Jiangnan University Sports Association also had five resolutions and informed the Referees Association by letter. The details are explored below.

Resorting to Law to Manifest Human Rights: When the Referees Association convened, all members were extremely indignant, believing that the Jiaotong University authorities had not given the offending students severe punishment, which was deeply regrettable. Since the school authorities had no solution, they had no choice but to resort to law to manifest human rights. Three members were immediately elected to form a special committee to take full responsibility for dealing with this extraordinary incident. The special committee has entrusted lawyer E Sen to handle the case. After discussing the matter with lawyer E for several days, it was decided to file a lawsuit in two parts, criminal and civil. The criminal part will directly sue the perpetrators, and the civil part will sue the president of Jiaotong University. As for who the perpetrators are, it is said that the association does not need Jiaotong University to hand them over, as they have already been witnessed by many people, and they will not be allowed to escape the law. Witnesses and material evidence are all ready. Furthermore, according to a spokesperson for the association, the association originally intended to settle the matter peacefully and did not want to expand the incident, but after waiting quietly for many days, they only heard the sound of "investigation" but did not see the reality of "punishment," so they felt that they could no longer tolerate it and were willing to make the greatest determination to seek the upholding of the law and can also use this to deal with and prevent future problems. In addition, the association felt that member Shen Guoquan could not prevent the incident from happening and was not responsible during the incident. After the incident, according to reports from many members of the association, he remained indifferent, without any spirit of seeing justice and acting bravely or helping each other in times of trouble. In view of Mr. Shen's two positions, they felt that he was not in line with the spirit of the association. Furthermore, they felt that Mr. Shen's letter to the Referees Association lacked the true spirit of sports. Although it was called an apology, it was mostly a defense, with the entire text mentioning nothing more than how Jinan University was stealing the ball and why the referee was beaten, as if Shen Huichun's beating was caused by the stealing of the ball. Although the words "apology" were uttered at the end, it was very reluctant. Carefully considering the meaning of the full text, it was no different from a statement of reasons for Shen Huichun's beating. The members of the association saw this situation and felt that he was no longer a comrade, so they also resolved to give him severe punishment. First, the association will send a letter to Mr. Shen, reporting the content of the resolution. If Mr. Shen believes that he is not satisfied within ten days after receiving the letter, he can be given the opportunity to respond, and then the special committee will review the matter. Otherwise, it will be executed upon expiration of the time limit.

Jiangnan University Sports Association Resolves on Five Items: After the unfortunate incident occurred, the Jiangnan University Sports Association also convened an executive meeting and resolved on five measures, and informed the China Sports Referees Association by letter: "Dear Sirs, Jiaotong University and Jinan University competed in the Jiangnan University soccer championship at the Jiaotong University stadium on the 16th of this month. Mr. Shen Huichun of your association was invited to officiate. Unfortunately, a dispute occurred at the end of the game. We convened an executive meeting on the 24th of this month (Sunday) and resolved on the following measures to resolve the matter: (1) A letter will be sent to Jiaotong University requesting reimbursement of medical expenses. (2) A letter will be sent to Jiaotong University to apologize to the Referees Association and Mr. Shen Huichun. (3) Jiaotong University will be suspended from participating in various competitions of the association for one year (from January 1, 1934). (4) A letter will be sent to the Jiaotong University authorities to severely punish the perpetrators. (5) A letter will be sent to the Referees Association to apologize and report the measures decided by the association. Furthermore, we intend to formulate permanent measures regarding the punishment of those who beat referees, but due to time constraints, we were unable to do so. We will make a final decision after the spring semester begins next year. This is specially reported to you, and we hope that your association will give us assistance in the future. Sincerely, the Jiangnan University Sports Association, December 26th."

Pucheng Leaves a Stain

—Lost to Mailing Last Night—

Players Punch Referee

Write Letter of Repentance and Apology

The Korean Pucheng University basketball team played its final game in Shanghai last night against Mailing at the China Basketball Hall. Although Pucheng lost, their performance was better than in previous games, with Mailing winning 42-33. However, after the game ended, player number eight (this player never appeared in the game, so his name is unknown) punched referee Shu Hong for no reason. Shu was furious and demanded that the team hand over player number eight. The team was adamant and initially refused, but Association executives and Referee Association President Yue Xiurong, etc., believed this was a deliberate insult and insisted that player number eight be handed over. At that time, Shen Guoquan intervened and eventually handed over player number eight. Negotiations took place in the Association's writing room for a long time. Association leaders Shen Siliang and Shu Le decided on two possible solutions: player number eight must write a letter of repentance, one copy to be kept by the Association and one copy to be sent to the president of Pucheng University. If this solution was not accepted, then player number eight would be handed over to the police. The team initially refused both options. After more than an hour of negotiation, Shen Siliang drafted a letter of repentance and had player number eight sign it under the name "Rong Jin." However, it was found that there was no such name on the team, clearly indicating that he had changed his name to deceive. The team's spirit in the first three games was exhausted. Unexpectedly, this farewell game last night left a stain, which is truly despised. In recent weeks, large and small disputes have arisen in the sports world, truly a troublesome time.

United Cup Table Tennis Scheduled to Start

—January 5th Next Year—

The Second United Cup Team Table Tennis Championship, organized by the Shanghai China Table Tennis Federation, is scheduled to begin on January 5th next year. Each night's matches will start promptly at 7:30 PM. Teams that are ten minutes late will be considered to have forfeited. Referees will be rotated between the two teams. The winning team is responsible for submitting the match results to the Association for registration after the match, in order to finalize the score. The deadline for submission is three days, after which the results will be invalid. A total of twenty-eight teams are participating in this year's event. Based on a single round-robin competition, 378 matches must be played. Participating teams should make every effort to avoid changing dates or forfeiting without reason, in order to avoid delaying the schedule and to emphasize the spirit of competition.
