Page 13

Free Talk

On Silence

— Wu Xi

In 1924, Mr. Zhou Zuoren once used three sheets of paper to advocate "silence," but he was not opposed to "noise," but because of "helplessness," saying "this is the appropriate method for China now." Mr. Zhou finally used "three sheets of paper," which shows that "silence" is ultimately an impossible thing.

Mr. Du Heng said that in this era, only clever people are "silent," but clever people are very few after all.

"Silence" can only be achieved by great sages and great men. The world is full of talkative fools; that's what I think.

In fact, what kind of pain is there in "silence"? Concretely, I can't really say. Mr. Wang Tongzhao, in the preface to his poetry collection "This Era," said, "The more feelings one has, the less one can write, the emotions that cannot be sorted out, the dramatic movements of the era that are not easy to set off, so one is willing to be silent, and this is truly a kind of deep depression! I think being able to cry, being able to shout, being able to sing, laugh loudly, or even being able to say a few witty remarks, or even chaotic吵, one's depression can be relieved somewhat. This is like vomiting and excretion in severe cholera, even if the body feels empty, at least the spirit can get temporary comfort." I think this can be borrowed for explanation. The lack of promotion of the "silence" style, viewed from this, has a long history.

Here, I think of Mr. Lin Yutang's compromise on the matter, advocating "humor," which is not without reason.

On Realistic Novels and the First-Person Writing Style

— Mu Mutian

Now, our young people can no longer find comfort in the ivory tower. The environment turns their eyes to reality, making them pay attention to the suffering of the masses. In the field of literature and art, they want to realistically express the life of hunger and cold of the masses.

In recent days, while sick, I have superficially read some young people's novels. As a result, I feel this phenomenon more deeply. This realistic tendency is indeed a symbol of an era.

However, one thing makes me deeply dissatisfied: that is, some young writers, in their hearts, want to realistically depict society, but because they use the first-person writing style, they reduce the truthfulness of those novels.

Since the style of Chinese novels has not yet been truly established, it is naturally excusable that those young writers make this mistake. When encountering a lot of material, and at the same time not finding the best form to express this material, to properly装装, they blindly use the old form. And the first-person writing style commonly used by romanticists is also used by them. Is this first-person writing style suitable for modern realistic novels? It seems that no one has discussed this yet. This may prove that those young writers are still romantic to some extent.

However, this tendency must be corrected. This tendency will turn the living reality in the novel into a mechanical formula.

There are quite a lot of works with this tendency. Now, let's just take Ms. Cao Ming's "Tilted" (Literary and Art Period 2) as an example. Naturally, judging from that "Tilted," Ms. Cao Ming is a very promising young writer. However, precisely because her future is bright, her shortcomings need to be corrected even more. Naturally, judging from that "Tilted," Ms. Cao Ming wants to try her best to grasp reality. However, precisely because of that reason, it exposed even more that her first-person writing style is not suitable for the subject matter, and reduced the truthfulness of the work.

Great realistic writers, such as Stendhal, Balzac, Flaubert, Zola, etc., rarely or never used the first person in their works. That kind of first-person confessional technique cannot express the objective complex reality. If you compare the novels of Musset, George Sand, with the novels of Flaubert and Zola, you can know the similarities and differences.

Writing about workers and farmers in the first person is very difficult to make the article 丨丨that article is the character's confession丨丨suitable for the identity of the protagonist 丨丨confessor丨丨. For example, "Yang Ma's Diary," you can tell at a glance that it is fictional. Yang Ma's life can be objectively described. However, to ask Yang Ma to write that beautiful diary is comical. That is the author's conceptual fiction, not reality. Moreover, it is not easy for a protagonist to see all aspects of a story.

This kind of first-person writing style easily makes the author idealize his characters, and even idealize them excessively. For example, in "Tilted," the heroine is a maid, but the author wrote her as a poet: "In the three months I was idle, I constantly produced many hopes and beautiful illusions, but they all sank into the gloomy and verdant 魔窟-like seabed like ships hitting reefs in the sea," "Su Qi felt the lonely and poor sorrow of the desert island," and so on. Many of these words, I am afraid that not only a female worker cannot say or imagine, but even liberal arts students may not be able to say this kind of vivid and colorful words. This kind of beautification and idealization is harmful to the truthfulness of art.

Now, isn't there a kind of disharmony between form and content in many works? If so, it needs to be overcome urgently.

Book Talk (Continued)

— Junzhi

(V)

Therefore, book lovers not only love books, but also like to beautify their reading life, such as the location of the study mentioned in Mei Gong's words. Li Rihua, in "Miscellaneous Notes from the Purple Peach Pavilion," once had a design for a study, which read:

The study should be located in a winding place in the stream and mountains. The structure should be limited to three rooms, with an upper floor to view the clouds. A hundred bamboos should be planted on all sides to attract the clear wind. A pine tree should be planted on the south side to hang my moon. An old regret is slumped, with low branches entering the window; fragrant grass and moss cover the bottom of the steps. Taoist and Buddhist books should be placed in the east room, Confucian books in the west room. In the center, in addition to the horizontal table, famous calligraphy and paintings should be placed. White rice and fish soup should be served for breakfast and dinner, famous wines and fine teas. A strong man should guard the pavilion, rejecting worldly interactions. If this continues for ten years, Zhong Yao, Wang Xizhi, Gu Kaizhi, and Lu Tanwei will be unknowable, but they will certainly not be inferior to Yu Shinan, Chu Suiliang, Wang Wei, Hua Yuan, and others.

The fantasies of a book madman can be seen here. However, whether the results of "ten years like this" will achieve what he expects is a question, with a smile.

"Reeds are green, white dew turns to frost"

— Cao Juren

丨丨Lecture at Shanghai Daxia University

"Reeds are green," a poem from Qin Feng. That is a love song. According to my speculation: When that man sent his lover back, the two walked along the river for a while, holding the long leaves of the reeds and standing facing each other for a while; the woman finally crossed the river, and they parted. After a long time, the woman never came back, maybe not even a single message. The man walked back and forth alone by the river, feeling restless in his heart; suddenly he saw the long leaves of the reeds, covered with a layer of frost; those long leaves pierced his heart, so he sang in a low voice:

"Reeds are green, white dew turns to frost.

The so-called beloved, is on the other side of the water;

Going upstream to follow her, the road is difficult and long;

Going downstream to follow her, she seems to be in the middle of the water!"

Suppose someone asked in a daze: "Why didn't the man cross the river to see his lover?" Maybe the woman's father was a moralistic gentleman who didn't allow them to love freely, not even to徘徊 outside the window, so he had to suffer from lovesickness by the river.

Falling in love, loving each other, missing each other, is a very ordinary and easily obtained experience for everyone, so writing love into poems occupies the most component in literary themes. Young men and women who are just entering the door of literature also prefer to read these kinds of themes, and there are many writers in Shanghai who make a living by writing these kinds of works. Since it is such a common and easily known theme for everyone, it should be very easy to write; why does this love poem by an unknown writer, "Reeds are green," let him walk alone through the ages? And why, three thousand years later, this lovesick patient's love song, when read after thousands of years, still "first gets my heart"? This is what I want to talk about today.

To open our heart bags in front of our lover, so that she understands our enthusiasm, is an extremely difficult task. Will you write thousands of words of love letters? Or hundreds of lines of poems? Maybe you will fail, completely fail. The best way to express love is not to write a word, not to say a word; silently the two lean on each other and walk on the grass, a crescent moon follows behind, honeysuckle sends a dark fragrance; at this time, each other's hearts are beating, cheeks are hot, eyelids are flowing, is there a more complete way to express it than this?

However, the expression of "not using a word, but naturally elegant" makes everyone feel unhappy; they must kneel on the ground and say: "I love you," or write on the stationery "I quietly belong to you," only then is it considered happy. Mr. Zhou Zuoren once said: "We somersault several times on the grass outside the door, imagining that the beauty on the high building is watching, which is very happy, is a method; anyway, she will not see it, so stop somersaulting, and lie on the grass to watch the clouds, this is also a method." Most of us ordinary people probably take the former method. (Those who do not somersault but 着 clouds are saints.)

Since you have to somersault to be happy, then the pattern of somersaulting appears. Poets express emotions, there are three patterns of赋比兴, this poem "Reeds are green" uses the pattern of "兴". The former people explained the meaning of "兴", saying that it is "borrowing things to evoke兴"; (Liu Eyun: "The text is exhausted but the meaning has餘, it is 兴," Li Yuyun: "Touching things to evoke feelings is called 兴, feelings are attached to things.") The long leaves of the reeds were originally unintentionally picked by each other at the time of farewell; when徘徊 by the river, these long leaves were the first stimulus to break into the mood, so he started writing from them, using them to express this emotion of lovesickness. For example, this round stool is too plain and unremarkable; but if my lover used to sit here often, but now she is dead, as soon as I see this round stool, I can't help but feel sad and shed tears, and mournfully chant: "Stool! Stool!" It seems that all the pain in my heart is entrusted to this plain and unremarkable round stool, and it seems that thousands of strands of pain must start from the round stool. Therefore, "Reeds are green, white dew turns to frost" and "The so-called beloved, is on the other side of the water" these two completely unrelated things, the poet connects them together, and we don't find it strange at all. (Zheng Yuzhong said: "The call of the osprey, is a temporary兴 for the poet, what he sees is here, and he feels it in his heart without planning it," which is what it means.)

Two Brothers (73)

— Authored by Maupassant, Translated by Li Weike

(8)

When Zhe'an returned to his own home, he collapsed onto a sofa. The sorrow and anxiety that made his brother imagine himself as a hunted beast, running and escaping, had a different effect on his lazy nature. It was as if his hands and arms were broken. He felt so weak that he couldn't move another inch, couldn't even go to bed. His body was as weak, tired, and bored as his soul. Unlike Bi'er, he was not struck by the purity of parental love, by the secret dignity that harbored a proud heart. Instead, he was overwhelmed by the blow of fate, which simultaneously threatened his most cherished interests.

When his soul finally calmed down, when his thoughts finally became clear again like water that had been stirred and then settled, he examined the situation that had been revealed to him. If he had heard the secret of his origins in a completely different way, he would have been angry and deeply saddened. But after arguing with his brother, after the violent and crude accusation that had shaken his nerves, his mother's sad confession left him with no strength to resist. The shock of compassion that was given to him was so severe that, under an irresistible emotion, he conquered all prejudices and all the sacred sensibilities of natural morality. Moreover, he was not a man of great resistance. He didn't like to fight with anyone, especially not with himself. So he let go, and driven by an instinctive tendency, by a natural love for peace, for a gentle and tranquil life, he immediately worried about the chaos that would occur around him and strike him at the same time. He foresaw that these upheavals were inevitable. In order to break these upheavals, he decided to meet them with superhuman efforts full of energy and activity. This difficult question must be resolved immediately, not tomorrow, because he sometimes had that strong need for immediate decision, a need that formed all the strength of those who cannot persevere. His lawyer's mind, accustomed to handling and studying complex situations and internal family problems that cause disputes, immediately discovered all the influences that were about to occur in his brother's soul condition. He involuntarily, almost from a professional point of view, considered the sequel to this matter, as if he were settling accounts with customers regarding future relationships after suffering a mental blow. Of course, continuing to have contact with Bi'er was impossible for him. It was very easy for him to avoid his brother by staying at home, but their mother could no longer live in the same house as her eldest son either.

So he lay motionless on the cushion, thinking for a long time. He thought of some plans and then abandoned them, without finding a satisfactory one.

But he was suddenly stimulated by a thought: Would a person who cherished his reputation keep the property he had received?

He initially answered, "No," and then decided to donate it to the poor. Although it was a very regrettable thing, he had no choice but to do it. He could sell his furniture, work like others, work like all newcomers. This majestic and painful decision spurred him on. He stood up and pressed his forehead against the glass window, looking outside. He originally had no money, and he was becoming moneyless again. In any case, he wouldn't starve. His eyes gazed at the gas lamp across the street. Just then, a woman returning home late walked by on the sidewalk, and he suddenly thought of Mrs. Lu Zuimi. He was deeply shaken by the cruel thought that arose. All the desperate effects that his decision would have appeared before him at the same time. He had to give up this woman, give up his happiness, give up everything. Could he do that? Now that he had promised to marry her? She had agreed to his proposal when she knew he was rich. Even if he had no money, she might still agree to him; but did he have the right to ask her, to force her to make this sacrifice? Wouldn't it be better to keep the property temporarily as a pledge, and then return it to the poor in the future?

Overview of the Daily Necessities Market (2)

(Xinan)

Vegetarian food has recently become popular, following the trend of believing in Buddhism. Vegetarian restaurants can be found in places like Chenghuang Temple, Daxin Street, Dongxin Bridge, and the vicinity of Sanma Road. However, the more exquisite vegetarian restaurants are undoubtedly Gongdelin and Jue Lin. Gongdelin was originally on Beijing Road, but since the houses there were converted into the Lake Society, it moved to Park Road. Jue Lin was originally on Wangping Street, but since that area became the center of the news industry, it also moved to the intersection of Xihui Road and Songshan Road. Eating vegetarian food, in terms of learning Buddhism, is of course to refrain from killing, so as to avoid the cycle of cause and effect and repeated reincarnation. However, like the Western advocacy of animal protection, the result must also lead to vegetarian food. Otherwise, if you only advocate protection verbally, and do not hesitate to slaughter animals to satisfy your appetite, how can this be the way to protect animals? Therefore, if you want to thoroughly protect animals, you must be vegetarian. For the time being, let's put aside refraining from killing and protecting animals. Even from the perspective of personal hygiene, it is better to eat more vegetarian food. Fish is easy to spoil, and meat is easy to spoil, so more people eat vegetarian food in the summer, which is precisely the reason. Ancient people strongly advised against eating foods that were smoked, roasted, or burned, saying that they could damage the stomach and intestines and easily cause carbuncles and boils. These words were not researched from science, but crystallized from experience, so of course they have some truth. However, some people say that foreigners eat a lot of smoked and roasted food, but they are not often seen suffering from carbuncles and boils. Does this mean that the words of the ancients are not credible? I am not a foreigner, so I have no way of knowing the situation in the abdomens of foreigners, but from my own experience and observations, I deeply feel that the words of the ancients are still not obsolete. Why is this? If we eat a lot of meat, we always feel uncomfortable in our abdomen, unless we have a strong stomach and intestines, but eventually we will get sick. What is the reason for this? Because this kind of food is not easy to digest and accumulates in the stomach and intestines, it will naturally produce toxins that enter the blood and spread throughout the body, which is called autotoxicity. If you don't get internal diseases, you will suffer from external symptoms. You see, foreigners often take laxatives and intestinal lubricants, and they must eat fruit after every meal, precisely to use the power of medicines and fruits to clear stagnation, but this is not a fundamental solution. Because the power of the medicine will cause inertia over time, and the natural ability to digest will weaken; fruit is not entirely suitable to be eaten with meals. In our country, there is a prohibition against eating fruit after meals, believing that sudden heat and sudden cold are not suitable. This shows the difference in preferences between the East and the West. It also shows that our country's diet, which emphasizes grains and vegetables and slightly includes meat, is the most hygienic method, which the West cannot match. First, various nutrients can be blended and absorbed comprehensively; second, most of the vegetarian food is plants, which are rich in chlorophyll and have the natural function of lubricating and unblocking the intestines. If you don't believe it, you can try it. If you eat vegetarian food once or twice after eating meat for a long time, the effect will be immediate. Therefore, vegetarian food does occupy an important position in hygiene. (To be continued)

Pinggaoer 127.50, Down 1.50, 25.10

Aomula 156.00, Down 0.50, 30.80

Bailuoxi 180.75, Down 0.25, 35.60

Grain: River Rice Market Dull, Sales Stagnant

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the supply showed a slight increase, with over 50 boats (over 7,000 shi) arriving at various wharves. Due to the approaching Lunar New Year, finance and shipping companies declared a suspension of business, including rice dealers, grain shops, and upper-level wholesalers. Consequently, only small-scale transactions occurred, resulting in a very quiet market situation. The market presented a stagnant picture. It is heard that the Shanghai market will be closed for two days during the Lunar New Year, leaving little hope for any turnaround in the coming days. The market for thick japonica and Duyang pointed rice remained similar to before, with prices unchanged. Yinbian rice also remained stable.

(North Shanghai) Over 40 boats arrived. Sales of various types of rice remained sluggish. White japonica, white yuan, Yangdu, Bujiang, and Xian rice remained firm. Early thin rice and Yin yuan remained stable.

Customer Xian Rice: Supply and Sales Both Slow

—Ningbo Merchants Inquire Slightly—

Yesterday, the customer Xian rice market experienced minimal arrivals and sluggish sales. Local rice dealers rarely inquired about customer Xian rice. Dealers from Fujian province uniformly suspended operations, and those from the north made no purchases. However, Ningbo merchants took the opportunity to make small purchases, including 120 bags of Jiangxi machine-processed late rice at 7.30 yuan and 100 bags of Hunan machine-pressed oil rice at 7.15 yuan. There were no other transactions. The market price was similar to the previous day. As the recent market price had already reached the bottom, and supplies were scarce, cargo owners were unwilling to sell at lower prices.

8,000 Bags of Future Flour Delivered This Month

Yesterday, futures flour trading was suspended for delivery. There were no transactions for either futures or spot flour. The delivery of this month’s futures flour has been fully completed, with a total of 8,000 bags delivered to the warehouse, including 7,000 bags of Maigen flour and 1,000 bags of Xiangxin flour. All were warehouse warrants recovered by northern merchants and hoarders.

Lower-Grade Yellow Beans Rise by Two or Three Cents

Yesterday, the yellow bean market was stable. Upper and middle-grade beans remained ostensibly stable but subtly weakened. However, there was slightly more activity in the purchase of lower-grade beans by factories, causing the market to rise by two or three cents. A total of six or seven cars of various beans were traded. Inland merchants purchased one car. Local trading amounted to three or four cars. Merchants from Xiamen inquired about 100-200 bags for export, including three cars of Zhengyangguan beans priced at 3.50-3.44 yuan, two cars of Guide beans priced at 3.45 yuan, and three cars of Yingzhou beans priced at 3.35-3.26 yuan. Three cars of Suixikou beans were priced at 3.30-3.27 yuan, and four cars of Bengbu beans were priced at 3.23-3.17 yuan.

Sugar Market: Domestic Green Sugar Opening Prices Continue to Ease

Yesterday, the sugar market still showed no sign of improvement. The Sugar Association quoted 24 for raw coarse white sugar at 19.50 yuan, down another 0.1 jiao. Re-exported goods were quoted at 6.75 yuan, at the original price, but without transactions, and further declines were expected. No. 20 medium coarse white sugar had no transactions, quoted at around 19.4 yuan. Nos. 8 and 9 Dutch red sugar were quoted at 15.7 yuan, unchanged. Taikoo sugar remained stable, with B mark at 20.15 yuan and CW mark at 20 yuan. Zhenji cotton white was quoted at the original price, with No. 1 at 18.55 yuan, and the rest discounted. The opening price of sliced green sugar also decreased. Over 200 boxes were traded yesterday, priced at 9.6 yuan, down 0.4 yuan from before. Over 100 pieces of Chaozhou green sugar were also offered, slightly down about 0.1 yuan, at 13.3-12.7 yuan. Another 280 pieces of new Diao green sugar arrived and were still being declared, and it is expected they can be cleared and offered tomorrow, with the possibility of further easing prices.

North-South Goods: Xingquan Longan Water Freight Increases

Cost Pressure Will Increase Accordingly

Xinghua Quanchuan longan has seen no continuous arrivals due to transport difficulties since the Fujian unrest. A certain company has chartered a foreign ship named "Shenyou," which has sailed to Xingquan to load longan. According to yesterday's telegram, it will be transported down soon, but the water freight has increased by 50% compared to before, thus increasing the cost. There is hope for improvement in the market later on.

Piece Goods: Only Sporadic Sales of Woolen Fabrics

As the end of the year approaches, all industries are looking to finalize their accounts. Woolen fabric trading is therefore quiet. Yesterday, the market at the guild was sluggish, and prices were chaotic. Transactions were mostly sporadic. Western-style suits, including fancy woolens, overcoat woolens, plain thick woolens, Melton cloth, and riding breeches woolens, saw relatively more active trading. Felt and shoe factories showed strong purchasing power, but only for sporadic amounts. Prices failed to rise due to the current period. There were still sporadic purchases of domestic wide and narrow camel hair at 1.6 yuan, and also some transactions of artistic plain camel hair at over 2 yuan.

Silk and Tea: Overseas Silk News Still Unchanged Yesterday

New York White Filature Has Prices But No Market. The New York raw silk market has recently seen active selling of silk holdings by general importers due to the approaching year-end and fears of global economic panic. Furthermore, excessive dumping of Japanese silk has led to no inquiries for Chinese silk. According to news from local American silk merchants such as Qianli, the current inventory of Chinese silk in New York reaches 3,700-3,800 bales. Grade B white filature is quoted at a strong US$1.4 per pound for a 83% evenness, which is 8-9 cents higher than the standard Japanese silk price. Converted to Chinese currency, the price per bale is only around 500 yuan, but there is still price but no market.

Douppion Silk Sales Not Quiet. Douppion silk sales have not been quiet recently. Although local single cocoon silk factories have all suspended operations, the Fulun Douppion Silk Factory is still working. Last week, the British mail steamer transported 40 bales of douppion silk for export to England for transshipment to India.

Rayon Inventory in Shanghai: 3,000 Cases. Imports of European and American rayon have not been smooth recently, and the inventory in Shanghai is sparse. According to checks, the total inventory of various sales agents is only about 3,000 cases, all stored in customs warehouses in Pudong due to tax payment issues. As for current spot sales, due to the approaching year-end and tight credit, various merchants have temporarily suspended purchasing, and the market is quiet.

Yellow and White Filature Silk Sales Desolate. The Christmas holiday has just passed, and overseas silk news remained unchanged yesterday. Yokohama Japanese silk prices were expected to rise. Although various European and American firms in Shanghai sent out filature telegrams yesterday morning, the prices demanded by various manufacturers were too high, making it difficult to extend the contract period. The market remained quiet. Only eight bales of yellow and white filature silk were purchased by inland silk shops yesterday, and prices remained weak.

Needle and Xiu Mei Teas See Slight Sales

Yesterday, in the foreign merchants’ tea market, English firms such as Tongfu and Yihuo slightly increased their purchases of domestic Needle, Xiu Mei, and other green teas to replenish their stocks. A total of 75 cases were negotiated city-wide, sold for 32 yuan, a decrease of 2-3 yuan compared to before. There were still no inquiries for Zhen Mei and Pearl Tea. Due to poor sales to foreign merchants, domestic factories have been suspending operations one after another, and the market situation is desolate.

Supplement to the Shen Bao Local Edition

Commentary

Human Inertia

— Wei Ba

Walking on the street, I heard vendors shouting about selling both the old lunar calendar and the new solar calendar. This couldn't help but evoke a feeling: humans are truly creatures of inertia.

The purpose of a calendar is originally to verify the dates between each other, but it is taken for its universality, regardless of national boundaries. So, since there is already a solar calendar, for the sake of convenience, there is no need to preserve that ancient and unpopular "lunar calendar" and be complacent about it. However, some people would rather abandon "convenience" and choose "inconvenience." What reason can explain this? Other than saying it is due to the inherent inertia of humans.

Human inertia is not limited to this. Apart from the old conservatives who keep their braids and inscribe "Spring King First Month," what is seen in daily life in society, such as weddings, still uses large red sedan chairs, drums, and music, parading down the street, preserving the relics of ancient predatory marriages. During funerals, many children wear ancient robes and gowns (also used at weddings), carrying hard plaques with inscriptions such as "Imperial Grant" and "Qing Gift." Funeral notices still have inscriptions like "Qing Feng XX." Resuming the reading of classics. Abandoning the universal vernacular Chinese and writing ancient and elegant essays in the style of the Tang and Song Dynasties. Recreating a republic, but then thinking of autocracy, etc., are all examples.

Human attachment to the past proves his weak creativity. The solution to problems lies in progress and creation, not in recollection and restoration. Humans can only find liberation in constant progress; recollection and attachment do not help the reality.

For example, if there is no food to eat, we can think of ways to make sure there is food to eat; if there are no clothes to wear, we can think of ways to make sure there are clothes to wear; if there is no work to do, we can think of ways to make sure there is work to do; all problems, except if you yourself do not want to solve them, are not entirely without solutions. But humans are content with simplicity, content with poverty, content with hunger and cold, allowing themselves to be dominated by one or two ambitious people, and then cannot help but shout "poor," shout "suffering," and cry to heaven. Abandoning one's own efforts and blaming society for not conforming to oneself, how can this be justified?

Ah, humans are originally so accustomed to laziness!

Modern Literati

— Li Zhai

Mr. Zhu Xiang, a poet with a high status in the new literary world, recently committed suicide by drowning. In this day and age, death is not a big deal, let alone the death of a literati who has nothing to do with wealth, power, and influence! So, I imagine that the death of Mr. Zhu Xiang, apart from evoking some sighs and sympathy among a few intellectuals who have a deep and melancholy experience of the meaning of life, will not bring tears of sympathy from those who wear light fur coats and warm belts and are at the height of their careers to "waste" on this unfortunate poet.

Because the death of the poet Zhu Xiang reminded me of the novelist Gu Zhongqi, who committed suicide three years ago, and the writer Peng Jiahhuang, who died of poverty and illness not long ago. The deaths of these three people have the difference between suicide and death from illness, but the sad plight of being strangled by the real society, haggard and exhausted, and dying with their aspirations unfulfilled is the same.

Using the clichéd phrase "literati are ill-fated" to mourn the defeated in the above-mentioned journeys of life is the most empty and vulgar thing to do. Originally, from ancient times to the present, among literati or poets, the lucky ones are few and the unfortunate ones are many; for the sake of convenience in speaking, it is not impossible to encompass and generalize it with the word "fate." But at the same time, it must be recognized that the "fate" or "ill-fate" of literati is not determined by heaven, but in reality is determined by people: half is determined by the preferences and needs of emperors, nobles, the rich, important people, and celebrities, and half is determined by the literati's own self-treatment. The great poet Li Bai also had a time when he was drunk in Chang'an and looked down upon the ministers, but it was not because he was "born under a lucky star" at that time, but because it happened to be a time of peace and prosperity, when drums of war were not sounding, and in the banquet atmosphere of kings and noble concubines, a poet like Li Bai, who was unadorned and naturally magnificent, was needed to embellish the occasion. However, Li Bai later could not avoid falling into obscurity and dying in decline; because he finally grew a few stubborn and proud bones, and in the eyes of the court and palace, he could not become a permanently pleasing decoration. In addition, among the literati of all dynasties, there were countless who were demoted, exiled, killed, or impoverished, while those who had good luck or "fate" were indeed very few.

In modern times, although the lifestyle of human beings has reached the ultimate in sound, light, electricity, and wondrous changes, the fact that literati or poets must find a way to "ascend the dragon gate" from the principle of "cooperating with the spiritual needs of the social ruling exhibition" has not changed slightly because of the "revolutions" that have been carried out more than once. This society, of course, still needs literati, but what it needs is definitely not poets like Zhu Xiang who faithfully sing the praises of nature or life, and express their artistic conception from their own perspective, but two other kinds: one is "skilled people" or "craftsmen" who are good at writing, who can write circular telegrams, eight-line poems, quatrains, couplets, and all kinds of social writings for people like "important people," "great men," and "celebrities," such as Rao Hanxiang, a specialist in four-six essay telegrams, and Bai Jianwu, who specializes in writing anti-Anfu clique and anti-Japanese traitorous telegrams. The other is a poet who is good at throwing out certain well-placed flattering words, such as Zheng Sujian, who is good at praising the saints, and the old man Fan Shan, who offered "General Zhang's Song of Pacifying Soldiers" two years before the "September 18th Incident" and thus received a reward of ten thousand gold. However, the kind of new poems written by the poet Zhu Xiang, with their light and ethereal artistic conception and light brushstrokes, are completely different from the literary and artistic style needed by the upper echelons of today. They can only be spoken to those who know, and cannot be spoken to "important people." They cannot be used as a "thunderous" manifesto, nor can they be used as a whitewash for peace. At the same time, they cannot be devalued to two yuan per thousand words to create wealth for booksellers and capitalists. Then, apart from being ignored by society and coldly treated by the general public, what "way out" has this cold society left for poets! Therefore, the poet's exhaustion, the poet's disillusionment, and even the poet's suicide are almost a predetermined conclusion of the facts.

Living in such a chaotic year and country, the way out for literati is originally like "a rat digging into a bull's horn, the more it digs, the tighter it gets." Looking forward and backward, recognizing the reality, there are only three ways out: one is to stand on the opposite side of the old social forces, racking one's brains to shout out for the oppressed and the circumstances of their struggles and resistance; the second is to stick to the tail of the old social forces and climb hard, reading those "Records of Mourning for Zeng and Zuo" and "What will happen to the people if my lord does not come out?" "Knocking bricks" or nauseating songs until they are memorized, relying on one's own writing and face to serve all the "raw and cooked Wei" powerful people. The third is to recognize one's own frustration as "the matter of course," neither advocating "contentment with poverty" nor seriously "hating life," and temporarily living a muddled life.

Unfortunately, the poet Zhu Xiang actually took the third path but could not extinguish his own wisdom. As a result, he became "without a way out." He finally could not overcome reality and committed suicide!

Expressing infinite condolences to Mr. Zhu Xiang, and at the same time hoping that if there are any frustrated writers among those who read my article, they will also be moved in their hearts and examine the path they have taken!

Gone Mad

— Shi Nong

"Zhang A'hu, I won't let you farm my land next year!" the landlord said sternly. Two eyes stared at a middle-aged farmer.

"Landlord... really..." The middle-aged farmer called Zhang A'hu pleaded in tears. "Really, God doesn't have eyes, my eldest son was taken away to be a soldier, and his life or death is unknown, my second son is sick... the harvest this year is bad, and the price of rice is cheap. I farmed twelve mu of land in total, and the rice I sold is not enough to pay back the money, the pancake money, redeem the pawn, and buy medicine. Now I barely managed to put together these few yuan, let me pay back some of the old debts! If I owe this until next year, I will definitely pay you back in the spring, let me still farm the land next year. Landlord, please have mercy on my whole family, I have been a tenant for more than ten years, and I have never owed you before when the harvest was good... Landlord... Landlord..."

"Don't be so long-winded!" The landlord became impatient. "I have already asked Peng A'hu to farm the land next year!" Saying that, he walked inside.

Zhang A'hu walked out of the landlord Li Squire's lacquered gate painfully in tears.

"Mom, it hurts! It hurts!" The sick child moaned in pain in the dark bed.

The peasant woman frowned and comforted her only remaining son A'Niu while crying.

"Good son, be quiet, it's okay, wait a while, your father will come back with the medicine, and you will be better after you take it."

"It hurts, it hurts!" The child still cried and moaned.

The peasant woman went to open the door painfully, waiting for her husband to come back.

The sky slowly darkened, and the child's crying gradually subsided. A black figure walked from afar, staggering. The peasant woman hurried over.

"A'Niu's dad! What happened?"

"Damn it! That landlord... hateful... the land for next year has been given to Peng A'hu to farm... damn it, that guy!..."

"You drank alcohol again, didn't you?"

"To hell with it! I'll drink two catties for nothing, and then we'll talk! To hell with it!... That landlord... that Peng A'hu thief... damn it!..."

"A'Niu's dad, what about the medicine?" The peasant woman asked him about the important matter.

"All the money was spent on alcohol!"

"You damn killer! You don't care that your son is so sick, you only know how to drink alcohol, I'll fight you to the death!" The peasant woman cried and pounced.

Suddenly, Zhang A'hu opened his eyes wide, clenched his fists, and punched his wife's forehead, saying in his mouth:

"You son of a bitch: You're good! ... I'll kill you, Peng A'hu!"

The peasant woman was so frightened that she ran into the door. Zhang A'hu also jumped in.

Page 16

Inside the door, the child's voice was calling "It hurts, it hurts!"

A week later, the whole village knew that Zhang A'hu had gone mad. There was one more small coffin in Tian Hengtou. (The End)

Wife

— Hao Qiu

Since I raised the banner of "rebellion," I have suffered the family's cruel "encirclement and suppression." Fortunately, I have received the sympathy and support of my sober-minded younger siblings, and I have broken through the extremely hot fire fight. However, at this time, I already have a nominal wife left at home, and because of the continued expansion and deepening of family conflicts, my younger brother has also risen up to demand freedom of marriage. In this way, the anti-feudal rule has been greatly revealed. Now, it has been seven or eight years, and my younger brother's old marriage contract has been cancelled before marriage, but the incident itself has not been restrained. Is it about severely punishing me, the "chief of the Rong," the "rebel"? But I am far from belonging to them.

My younger brother and sister each have their own crystallization products. My wife simply believes that I will definitely not grow a "tail," and that I am so proud that some people say that I am still a "loner" and that I always don't believe it. But when I can't get rid of my boredom, I will ask the servant to find a blind man to tell my fortune. She.

Originally, her fate was destined to be seen through at a glance by the "blind man." My mother knew that this third daughter-in-law would be the most capable person in the family in the future, so she gave the blind man a lot of money, and then sent a letter to report the good news and take her over early to receive her education, so as to show her great talents. Now, my mother has passed away, so of course only my mother's consultant - the blind man - can be consulted. In this way, she has spent six years and is now in her seventh year.

It is said that this time the fortune teller made a concrete conclusion: [There will definitely be two more "husbands" added, as long as this year passes]. However, the big premise, of course, is [breaking away from the disaster]. Passing this year is the goal set for [blank], but as far as I know, the addition of "two husbands" should be to change this original big premise to make it a bit possible.

It is also said that this time the fortune teller received a reward that exceeded my mother's by many times. And since that day, the poisonous and haggard face has occasionally had a faint smile from the depths of the heart pass over it.

It was about yesterday evening when the dusk had already spread and infiltrated the earth! A classmate came who was a new acquaintance but seemed like an old friend; after a short rest, he exclaimed as if he had made a big new discovery and stared at me! "Mr. Hao, are you married?" Because it was the first time we met, he used "Mr. Fa Xiang also." I said "yes" unnaturally, and then he came with a sentence, "You are a wife-killer." I lost my smile. "Look how high the corners of your eyes are," he came up with his "scientific" argument, as if he was afraid that I wouldn't believe him. I shook my head and said softly, "My words are accurate, your wife will not live long; last month, a certain civil servant's 'disaster' was said not long ago..." Again, he seemed to be so-called objective, and those who came with him also responded: "There is such a thing." Shadows fell on my face, and I imagined that I had something to say in my heart. After a while, he pressed forward again: "Your wife will die next year!" My mouth was dry from not saying much! After saying "definitely," he seemed to be afraid that I was anxious, "Fortune-telling is extremely difficult to see, the best or the worst fortunes seem to be not bad at all!"

I silently recited my fortune and my wife's fate, my wife's next year, two "next years," if there are two "next years" then she should live two more years, one plus one, is really equal to two! Since it is neither like the blind man's "next year" nor like the friend's "next year," I think it is a bit accurate! Isn't it said that there is such a thing as so-called eclecticism that can exist in the world now?

Between Life and Death

— Li Zhai

Recently, an Englishman named Phil Dam published a strange advertisement in the London Daily Express, expressing to all relatives and friends, "Instead of giving me wreaths after my death, it is better to take advantage of the present and give me cash!" After reading all this strange news, I couldn't help but close the newspaper and sigh, "As for Phil Dam, he is cynical and quite witty, but his understanding of the true meaning of life is still insufficient!" Why do I say this? Please see below!

In all ages and societies, the "sympathizers" who shed tears for the coffin are countless, while the good people who "help the poor and relieve difficulties" are originally very few. This is not because most people value death over life, but in the intangible philosophy of life, many people use the etiquette of reciprocity with deep meaning, and regard weddings, funerals, and celebrations as one of the "tactics" of people. Everyone is accustomed to doing the "icing on the cake" and regards helping people in need as a dangerous path. Gradually deduced, the result is of course "in prosperous times, there is a constant stream of traffic, and in times of decline, the door can be set up to catch sparrows." As for adding flattery or eulogy to the dead, whether the deceased is the old grandfather of a wealthy man or a traveler from a poor road, they are happy to give condolences, which is beneficial and harmless. Because, if the deceased himself or his son is of a higher status than oneself, then the words to mourn him prove that one's own communication is not "stiff," that one can "handle things" in public. If the deceased's status is below oneself, then putting one's own name on the eulogy can also prove that one is noble and prominent, but "does not forget old friends." If the deceased is one's own political enemy, or even if one has "helped a lot" in his death, then it is even more necessary to mourn him, first to show that one does not confuse public grievances with private feelings, and second to show one's own hidden pain of "I did not kill Bo Ren," which is the so-called "crocodile tears." Because of these three points, borrowing money from friends while alive often runs into walls everywhere, but sending funeral notices to collect wreaths and eulogies from people who are not close friends is often foolproof. Not only that, mourning death and pitying life have a big difference. Borrowing ten or five yuan from a friend, he will not "thank you in the newspaper" in fact, and it is inevitable that he will be "proud" once and come back to bother you a second time. Sending eulogies and wreaths to the dead is not the case. The "big name" is naturally marked high on the wreath or eulogy, and at the same time, the dead ghost will never bother you a second time. Therefore, there are many "benevolent gentlemen" who wave "a handful of tears of sympathy" to the dead who have already been buried, while those who open their wallets to help friends in need of food and clothing are few and far between!

What has been discussed above is the analysis of the psychology of the "sympathizers" who generally give gifts to the dead. At the same time, I want to expose one point, which is the psychology of the "filial sons and virtuous grandsons" who generally carry the dead to widely collect favors. In the sea of officialdom, where promotion and demotion are all ingenious, the death of parents is not simply a matter of mourning (or worry) and observing mourning customs. At the same time, in order to show off, especially to become famous, one must take the opportunity to use direct or indirect methods to get all the portraits, praises, inscriptions of the chairman, president, committee chairman, minister, and various celebrities and old masters, nail them into a very thick book, so that the dead man becomes a saint who "has virtue in his hometown," and the woman becomes a modern "Meng Tao" who is good at educating her children. In this way, not only will the dead smile in the nine springs (?), but the living will also have their "background" implied. Therefore, small things like defecating and eating, and big things like getting married and dying, are all "ingenious" in the upper class society of China.

There are too many "benevolent people" who flatter ghosts, and too few good people who save people. This is why China is in such a terrible state that it cannot be cleaned up!

Gate of Hope

— Wen

That was in June of this year. A friend named Zhang had his subsidy for the news agency he was running cut off due to the provincial government's "austerity policy," which put his livelihood in jeopardy. Naturally, he was struggling to start anew, but there were connections to exploit in Nanjing, and ways to consider back home. Should he return to his hometown, or seek opportunities in Beijing? This question mark kept battling in his mind, leaving him hesitant and indecisive. Finally, he came to me.

"Old Chen! I'm so bored! I've thought and thought about what I should do, but I still can't decide. If you have nothing else to do, let's go out and find someone to analyze characters or do divination... Of course, it's superstition, but it would make me feel better to waste two dollars on it! I'm just a mess at home, unable to figure out what to do..." Before my friend could finish explaining his intention, I stood up.

"Alright! I'll go with you. I might as well learn something from the fortune-tellers of Shanghai..." With that said, I put on my long gown and went out with him.

We got off at the New World and first went to a hotel on Tibet Road to find a very famous character analyst. Walking up to the third floor, our fortune-teller hadn't arrived yet. According to a teenage boy looking after the place, "Please have a seat, he'll be here in half an hour..." The fee was two dollars and twenty cents, which we paid as usual. Following the boy's instructions, we lit an incense stick and stuck it in the incense burner, and then shook out two character beads from the specially made "tool."

The fortune-teller was still not coming, so my friend and I took off our long gowns, wiping away sweat while observing the prices for character analysis, fortune-telling, and writing services hanging on the walls, as well as the slogan "Close friends and relatives, cash only." Mr. Zhang, always meticulous, had written a summary of the reasons for seeking character analysis to avoid any language barriers during the conversation, so that it would be clear at a glance. After waiting for half an hour, and with two more customers arriving to "seek guidance," the fortune-teller finally arrived leisurely. While taking off his long gown, he greeted us, repeatedly saying, "Sorry for the wait! I'm very sorry!"

After the usual pleasantries of "May I ask your name, and where is your esteemed residence..." the gentleman wiped the glass on the writing desk and poured water onto the brush from a large inkstone that looked somewhat like a "Han brick." He then enlarged and copied the characters on the character beads onto the glass.

The characters were "忠" (zhong, loyalty) and "羊" (yang, sheep). The fortune-teller began to "get down to business."

"Based on these two characters, I can say with certainty that your business must be pursued from Nanjing to have any hope! Because if you break down the character '忠' (zhong), the '心' (xin, heart) plus a stroke becomes '必' (bi, must), which together means 'must succeed.' But it must be during the Xin You month of July, in just over half a month, there will definitely be good news... Returning to Anhui is hopeless. The character '回' (hui, return) is two '口' (kou, mouth) characters, and adding a '口' (kou) to '忠' (zhong) becomes '患' (huan, trouble), so pursuing things back home is probably not a good idea. The result will only be sighing at the 'ocean' (the character '羊' (yang) plus three drops of water, which forms the character for ocean). Character analysis is just a bit of inspiration. I'll be bold and say that whether it's accurate or not will be clear in July. At that time, I'm afraid I'll be treated to a celebratory feast..."

"Extremely insightful! Thank you for your trouble!"

"It's nothing! It's nothing! You're too kind!"

After walking out of the hotel, I said with a smile, "You have to be clever to tell such nonsense!"

"It makes a lot of sense because I don't want to go back to Anhui at all!"

"A reassurance worth two dollars and twenty cents!"

We had breakfast at a restaurant on Nanjing Road. My friend still had two "Sun Yat-sens" (silver dollars) in his pocket, and he was still in high spirits. "Let's spend it all and go find 'Little Confused'!"

"Little Confused" was also one of Shanghai's "famous people," so we asked for directions to his place at a cigarette and paper shop on Guangxi Road.

We took a big detour and turned into Daqing Lane. In a downstairs room of a two-story building, we met Mr. Little Confused, who was hunched over, in his sixties, and balding. The room was filled with silver plaques and shields, and horizontal scrolls and couplets presented by figures like Wei Daofeng and Qu Yingguang. Mr. Zhang picked out the characters "爲" (wei, for) and "短" (duan, short) from a large pile of scrolls on the table. After explaining his intention, the old fortune-teller picked up his pen and "pronounced":

"Looking at these characters, your affairs will not succeed whether in Beijing or Anhui! Because the character '爲' (wei) has '爪' (zhua, claw) on top but no '瓜' (gua, melon), meaning there will be no results. And the bottom part is '似馬非馬' (si ma fei ma, like a horse but not a horse), '鳥不能飛' (niao bu neng fei, a bird cannot fly), which indicates a semblance of hope but ultimately no success. Moreover, half of the character '短' (duan) is '矢' (shi, arrow), and '矢' (shi) plus '走' (zou, walk) is '迭' (die, repeatedly), meaning repeated failures! So, now you can only wait quietly for an opportunity. There is too little hope at the moment! Too little!..."

After finishing his myth, the silver dollar was taken out and paid - one dollar and twenty cents.

"Little Confused made me even more confused! It's like he's memorized those dozens of words. Why 'like a horse but not a horse'? Why 'a bird cannot fly'? '矢' (shi) plus '走' (zou) is '迭' (die), 'repeated failures' - why not 'repeated successes'? Heh, '矢' (shi) plus '走 走' (zou zou), isn't that a character at all! Nonsense! Ugh!" My friend, upon leaving the door, recited this like a mantra all the way back.

New Business Sutras

— Jianren

Recently, commercial competition has become increasingly bizarre. In the past, there were "big sales" and the like, but only two or three times a year. There was also quite a bit of lively decoration, but never with the extravagance and cleverness of today. The intensity of the struggle for survival is evident, but in this battle to win over consumers, many geniuses, creators, and "new business sutras" are naturally emerging.

In this year of constant sales, it is not easy to win over customers. Even if the decorations are as lavish as possible, they can only attract idle onlookers. To make customers open their wallets and let the shiny gold coins flow out, you need to find another way. Therefore, this year's business sutras must have the following magic weapons: setting up a discount department; buy one get one free; two-hour sales; giving away brocade pennants, gift certificates, amusement park tickets, photography vouchers; and finally, giving away national salvation lottery tickets with a first prize of 500,000 yuan, redeemable by luck... Ah ah! Truly endless Shanghai prosperity and merchant ingenuity.

However, these are still ordinary business practices, and have not yet shed the airs of being a businessman. As for a groundbreaking page in the 1933 business sutras, I must recommend a certain merchant's gift of "classic books." This is truly beyond the expectations of ordinary people, and is elegant, morally upright, timely, and profitable all at the same time. This is indeed a new invention, worthy of the attention of the business community and those outside it. And the foresight of a certain merchant makes us ordinary people admire them to the point of prostration. Magistrate Dong of Funing County ordered the recitation of the "Classic of Filial Piety," which was once praised as a good story. Now, it cannot be exclusively beautiful. "The preciousness of the classics can be imagined from this." Logical! Logical! Another gift of 10,000 copies is truly generous of the boss! I have nothing to say.

However, from this, I can't help but think that after there is a Master Lu with pockmarks, there might be a Master Huang with pockmarks. The development of this business sutra has a very broad future. However, although the magic weapon is the same, different methods and skill levels will produce different results. Some people like to read the Four Books, but others like to read the history of sex. People's [gap] [gap] and [gap] [gap] are different, but they should not be [gap] [gap] used rigidly. Now, I will promote and expand this classic, and the "holy books" and "registers" that can be given away are as follows:

I think: Women's bookstores, cosmetics companies, women's English tutoring night schools, and the YWCA should give away a copy of the "Daughter Classic" for every one yuan spent, or for joining a tutoring class or becoming a member, limited to 20 million copies.

Children's bookstores and toy stores can give away a copy of the "Classic of Filial Piety," the more copies the better.

Hotels, ships, trains, and long-distance buses should give away "Travel Guides." Bathhouses and massage parlors should give away nude painting vouchers. Brothels and private houses should give away a copy of the New 606 Instructions or Dr. Zhang Jingsheng's History of Sex. Dance halls and movie theaters should give away a volume of Zhang Ziping's Triangular Love Novel as the most interesting. In addition, "holy books" and "registers" can be given away according to the nature of the "business," and the application is infinite.

In addition, gifts can be given to customers according to their age, gender, and status, to better suit their needs. For example, old women can be given a copy of the "Jade Box Record," old men can be presented with a chapter of the "Book of Supreme Induction"; young mistresses need the "Treatise on Safe Childbirth"; and young masters need to read the "Art of Getting Rich." All can be matched according to their needs, and I can guarantee that business will flourish. As for modern men and women, "modern youths," if they do not want to read the "classics," they can be given "a bunch of love letters" or "two bunches," a thick book of "beauty techniques," and a thin book on the art of controlling your wife or husband. I guarantee you will receive smiling faces and shiny foreign coins flowing out of their purses like water. Thus, the "way" of the new business sutras is complete. It not only promotes its own unsellable goods, but also does a business that second-hand bookstores could not have dreamed of. It also earns the beautiful names of "upholding morality" and "elegance," and the grateful tears of many old-fashioned people. Is there anything more beneficial in the world? This "new business sutra" is worthy of being greatly promoted and specially promoted. Therefore, I wrote "New Business Sutras."

Novel

Shanghai (30)

— Zhang Laosan

(43) The Sky of Shanghai

The gloomy weather, with clouds like a weight pressing down on one's head, gave people an unspeakable feeling of suffocation and depression. After Sister Hui left, the entire afternoon was spent in the office, with Xin Di, Little Huang and I sitting silently. Little Huang was indignant at the unconditional terms published in today's newspapers, saying, "This is simply outrageous! If I were the mayor, I would never agree! I would rather turn Shanghai into the desolate wilderness of fifty years ago! Look at the power of our people!" He kept extending his fan-sized fist.

"A weak country has no diplomacy, but there is still a chance to fight this time..."

A voice like breaking glass, "Extra! Extra!" flew past the door. As if we had been waiting for it, we all rushed out at the same time. On this usually quiet Rue de Bannes, there were clusters of people, each face marked with a question mark. If you bought an extra and tried to stand still on the street to read it, a crowd would quickly gather around you, and the crowd would grow larger and larger. This is how the clusters of people gathered.

Little Huang bought an extra—or rather, snatched it. He put the copper coin in the newsboy's hand and ran off. "Extra! Extra!" The trembling cry vibrated in the gloomy air, making people feel as if something terrifying was about to happen. As soon as I leaned forward, two people who hadn't managed to get an extra surrounded me.

"What? Are we going to fight?" one asked.

"I heard the conditions were agreed to!" the other replied, but the tone of his voice was not very trusting.

"Agreed to." Little Huang wanted to hand the newspaper to me, but the person who had asked intercepted it.

Back in the office, we turned on the electric light, and the two of us remained silent, of course, with the same distrust of the agreement. In the evening, Xiaofeng and Chongbian did not return. Sheng Di said they had gone to Zhabei to pick up relatives.

My heart was spinning like a wheel, and I couldn't fall asleep. In the middle of the night, the surroundings were as silent as death. I seemed to faintly hear gunfire. Little Huang jumped out of bed and said that Zhabei must have opened fire. He hurriedly got up, pushed open the window, and looked into the distance. A head poked out of the window across the street and asked loudly if we had heard anything.

"Gunfire!" Little Huang replied.

As he spoke, the sound rang out again. The disturbance lasted all night until dawn. The rattling sound of airplanes in the sky confirmed everything. Outside, there was a lot of talk about the Japanese suffering a defeat.

"Go to Zhabei!" Little Huang laughed triumphantly, "Look at the power of our people!"

I entrusted Xin Di to Afu and sent him to Gao Fei's house, telling him that we were leaving and asking Gao Fei to come to the office to settle things.

"I want to go to my sister's house," Xin Di said.

"Okay. Your sister will definitely come today. You can stay with your uncle." We left.

My cousin arrived at the office a few minutes after we left. Xin Di told her what we had said. She searched my bedroom for a while, and seeing that there was no note or anything, she leaned against the window and wept.

"Sister," Xin Di leaned against Sister Hui's side.

"Brother..." She stroked her brother's hair.

The rattling sound of airplanes filled the sky of Shanghai.

Film Special

Interview with Chinese Film Artists (30) (Continued from December 19th)

— Sha Ji

(13) Wu Cun, Director of "Wind" (Part 1)

I believe that readers are quite unfamiliar with this new figure. Although you have rarely had the opportunity to get to know him through his past works, in the near future, you will definitely be able to appreciate his artistic style in his "Wind."

In order to make it easier for readers to understand him, I will first give you a general introduction.

He is from Xiamen, Fujian, and is only twenty-nine years old this year. During the great Chinese turmoil of 1925, he edited the supplement of a newspaper in Xiamen. This newspaper should have a glorious place and history in the history of the Chinese revolution, but it was shut down due to the impact of the waves of darkness. From then on, he left his hometown in bloodshed and began to step into the Shanghai film industry.

As early as the age of fifteen, he devoted himself to the spoken drama movement. This was because the educational and business circles in Xiamen at that time vigorously maintained the public performance of new dramas every year during the annual and summer vacations, which lasted for two months. Therefore, there were many opportunities to perform at that time, which cannot but be the most memorable era for his personal drama cultivation.

Since joining the film industry in 1925, he continued for six years, from writing scene notes to assistant director. It was not until 1931 that he produced his maiden work, entitled "Blood Flower and Tears," which was produced by Fudan Film Company. In July of this year, he joined Lianhua No. 2 Factory, and his second work was this "Wind."

The following is a record of his conversation.

The morning of the third day after the winter solstice; the weather was still so warm, it was really strange weather. Walking on the pebble road next to Yanping Road, the faint fragrance of vegetables came from the vegetable garden on the right. People who have lived in the city for a long time cannot help but take a deep breath in this fresh atmosphere.

When I was about to reach the gate of Lianhua No. 2 Factory, I caught up with a young man in a suit. He had his hands in the pockets of his overcoat, and each of his armpits was carrying a grapefruit. Because he looked quite like my friend Dai Jun, I looked at him carefully, because Dai Jun and I had not met for several years. In the end, I ran ahead of him and reached the gate of the Second Factory. I asked the gatekeeper:

"Hey, is Mr. Wu Cun inside?" (To be continued)

Film Review

Review of "Vanity Misled"

— Yiqun

Walls of Gold

丨 Produced by Fox Company, screening at Great Shanghai 丨

This is an ugly history of a family, depicting an uncle snatching his nephew's lover, and a younger sister taking her older sister's lover. The main theme seems to be to expose the power of money, which ultimately cannot defeat true love. In the world, only those who can use true love can last, and only then can lovers be united. Those who use money for evil will ultimately be punished. The story is bland and unremarkable, just an old tune.

Now let's talk about other things.

First of all, regarding the central consciousness of the screenwriter; I think that the main theme of the play is to expose the evil consequences of buying love with gold, and to promote true love. Therefore, in addition to depicting the ugliness of the power of money, there should be a clear indication of love, so as not to focus on one thing and lose sight of the other. However, it is a pity that in this play, we only see that the copper and iron tycoon Gao Tong uses his power of money to do evil everywhere. We do not see where the true love between JeanieanieSattelea or Honey Satterl and BarnesRitchie is built. The love between the two sisters for Barnes, one by one, all seems very accidental, like "made in heaven," and like "love at first sight." After all, why do they love each other? What is the true love between them that is not built on money, and it is not expressed enough. Moreover, the combination of Barnes and Honey, and Jeanie and the copper and iron tycoon, are all given in a kind of forced coming together because of anger. Whether this combination of angry doctrine can be said to be love is, of course, the ultimate joke! Speaking of this, I recall that this is the opinion of the Americans, and I have nothing to say.

Secondly, regarding the director's technique, I think it is not bad. The division of scenes is very clean, the camera is very flexible, and several small comic scenes are readily available and very natural and appropriate. But it is a pity that the handling of the copper and iron tycoon's robbery and murder is too improper.

As for the performance, I don't think Sally Eilers is very special, but she can be called qualified. Ralph Morgen is still successful. He shows the ugly state of the idle and wealthy in society. Every move is very tasteful, and it makes people think of the typical characters they see and hear in their daily lives.

In short, although this play is not a successful work, it can still complete its task in exposing the ugliness of money.

Finally, Guan's translation of the name as "Vanity Misled" is really not appropriate, especially Jdanie is not translated as Jenny, but as Qin Qi, and Honey is not translated as Hong Ni, but as Hong Qi, which is also thought to be inappropriate. I hope that the organizers of Great Shanghai will pay attention to it.

The Boredom of Screen Lovers

— Huaming

This is the most unfortunate news in Hollywood in 1933. A famous Hollywood screen lover has now split up from each other and become a pitiful person in the sky of hatred in the film industry. This matter may occupy a page in the history of the film industry, causing future generations to feel a lot of emotion.

At first, when Janet Gaynor and Charles Farrell co-starred in "The Tide of Love," there were many rumors in Hollywood that Charles Farrell's contract with Fox had expired, and after "The Tide of Love" was completed, he would retire and live at home, and would no longer work for the film industry. Soon after this news was produced, it became a fact. Charles Farrell and Janet Gaynor broke up and ended their relationship as lovers on the screen. The occurrence of this accident caused people in Hollywood and other places who knew their status and history in the film industry to sigh very much.

Then there was the unfortunate thing between Jeanette MacDonald and Maurice Chevalier. The two of them in the Hollywood film industry, like Charles Farrell and Janet Gaynor, were called screen lovers, but they, like Charles Farrell and Janet Gaynor, unfortunately broke up. When Maurice Chevalier and Jeanette MacDonald were closest in the film industry, how envious they were. But now they are also separated, and people in Hollywood no longer recognize them as screen lovers. Indeed, they enjoyed the same luck and glory as Charles Farrell and Janet Gaynor, and at the same time have feelings that they cannot bear to look back on.

Strangely, although Charles Farrell and Janet Gaynor separated, Charles Farrell and his wife still lived happily and enjoyed family happiness, while Janet Gaynor divorced her husband, Liddell Beck. The separation of Maurice Chevalier and Jeanette MacDonald was just the opposite. Jeanette MacDonald and her husband were still happy in France, while Maurice Chevalier divorced his wife, Pony Fan Li. The endings of these two screen lovers happened to become a natural inverse proportion.

New Attempts in the British Film Industry

— Huang Yingdai

Compete with Hollywood for the World

Fairbanks has Joined the Cooperation

This is truly an important development in the British film industry. According to the latest news, London Films has joined forces with Fairbanks to organize a large-scale film company. British artists, technicians, and first-class American artists from Hollywood who are in leading positions will be recruited. This new organization will change the eyes of people all over the world, because in the past three years, Britain has removed a deep barrier and gradually broken away from the oppression of the American film industry. At present, British products have become the first in the world in terms of films needed by various countries other than American products.

Fairbanks' vision is very long-term. The things he is starting to do will soon be imitated by general entrepreneurs in the United States. Fairbanks' first film in England will be directed by Alexander Korda of London Films, and the film is titled Don Juan. Then he will re-shoot his successful silent film Zero as a sound film. His son will play a supporting role with him in this film. The first film to be shot is Catherine The Great of Russia, with Fairbanks Jr. playing the young Russian emperor and Elizabeth Paul Wagner playing Catherine.

Although the names of other new actors have not been announced, it is generally believed that five famous British actors will join this organization. They are Leslie Howard, Charles Laughton, Herbert Marshall, and Clifton Webb. Within the realm of possibility, Boris Karloff may also join. In the future, this group may build its own studio, but now it is shooting films at the Empire Studio.

Three years ago, British films did not occupy any position in the world, but now British films are being shown in all countries around the world like films from other countries. In future attempts, the British film industry has resolved to defeat the United States and completely take the Hollywood film industry into British hands.

"Flying Flower Village" is the First Shot of Four Plays

— Chu

In mid-January next year, Yihua Company stipulated that four plays should be filmed one after another. One is "Golden Age" directed by Bu Wancang, one is "Woman" directed by Shi Dongshan, one is "Flying Flower Village" directed by Zheng Yingshi, and one is "Love's Adulthood" directed by Ying Yunwei. But according to the decision of a crew meeting yesterday, Zheng Yingshi's "Flying Flower Village" has been ranked as the first shot. It will be put into production this week.

"Flying Flower Village" tells a tragic story about a train driver A Hua and his beautiful wife under the brutal forces of the current society. Because it focuses on exposure, this play is bound to be lively and stimulating. Everyone at the script meeting believed that this kind of play was quite valuable.

Anniversary Celebration Held in the Club

Jin Yan is a very warm-hearted man. Although he occupies the highest position in the Chinese film industry, he is very humble in his dealings with people. He is as kind and affectionate to his colleagues, even a tea house worker, as he is to his own brothers. At the Lianhua colleagues' party, he left his seat to serve dishes to his colleagues. Although this is not a big deal, it should be said to be an expression of his enthusiasm.

The New Year is approaching, and Jin Yan and Fei Mu have launched a New Year celebration in the Lianhua No. 1 Factory Club, preparing for everyone to gather together during the New Year. Fei Mu supplied various foods, Jin Yan supplied a large box of wine, and factory director Li Minwei and Liang Bocixing Shaomei and others also supplied items. Now, other colleagues are also enthusiastically participating. It is generally expected that the New Year will be lively enough.

The Two Rivers Women's School A Galaxy of Stars

Sun Yu, director of Lianhua Film Company's No. 2 Studio, is making further efforts after "Little Toys" with his film "The Athletic Queen." On the 19th, he borrowed the Two Rivers Normal School of Physical Education to film outdoor school scenes. Due to bad weather, there were no gains, but the next day the sun shone and everything went very smoothly. The actresses participating in the filming include Li Lili, Wang Moqiu, Wang Yan, and the newcomer Bai Lu, with Yin Xu making a guest appearance. The male actors include Zhang Yi, Shang Guanwu, Han Langan, Yin Xiucen, and Li Junqing, etc. These movie stars mingling with their "athletic queen" counterparts and galloping on the sports field truly create a dazzling spectacle like a galaxy of stars. On this day, dozens of shots were filmed throughout the entire day, only completing half of the school life scene. Therefore, they went again on the third day and filmed all day to finish this scene.

Film Novel

The Fire of Youth (2)

— Hou Feng

"The Fire of Youth" is burning in Commander Hu's mansion. Zhang Jisen, Da Xiong's secretary, has long been drooling over Ailian. However, Ailian already has He Mengxian in her heart. Therefore, she only feels disgust for Zhang Jisen.

One evening, when Mengxian had already put on his pajamas and was preparing to sleep, Ailian sneaked into his room and saw a half-length portrait of Xu Lanfen with the words "Mengxian's Kiss" written on it, which made her feel infinitely sad. She actually took down the photo and erased the word "kiss." Da Xiong returned home and saw Ailian being so affectionate with Mengxian in Mengxian's room, and couldn't help but be consumed by jealousy. Ailian took the initiative and walked over with Lanfen's photo, smiling and saying to Da Xiong:

"Look, isn't our future cousin-in-law beautiful!" leaving Da Xiong speechless again.

Da Xiong left home to go to the province to thank the commissioner. Ailian tried even more to seduce Mengxian. Another evening: Ailian called Mengxian to her room, saying that she wanted him to write a letter to the commander for her. At this time, Mengxian, although he knew that the magistrate had a wife, was not Liu Xiahui. How could he not be moved by this profound temptation? Therefore, under the development of this natural law, Mengxian gradually became estranged from Lanfen under Ailian's generous treatment. One day, Lanfen came to Hu's mansion to look for Mengxian, only to see Mengxian and Ailian sitting together having breakfast, but Ailian had her maid hide it from Mengxian and refused to see Lanfen, saying "Mr. He is not at home!"

This fire of youth is becoming increasingly serious. Zhang Jisen tried his best to alienate Mengxian and Ailian's relationship, and to make him reconcile with Lanfen. He went to Xu's house to see Lanfen, and was severely reprimanded by Lanfen. Later, her sister Huifen explained it to him and asked him to move out of Hu's mansion and leave Ailian. So, amidst the conflict of these two emotions, he agreed to Huifen's request—to move out of Hu's mansion, giving Lanfen a factual explanation. But when Mengxian returned to Hu's mansion and wanted to move out, Ailian refused. She said: "If you move out so hastily, how can I explain it to the commander when he comes back? He will definitely blame me for offending you, or even suspect that I am with you... How can I live like this?" Later, Mengxian decided to move out of Hu's mansion. He even wrote a letter of refusal to Ailian. But that letter was taken away by Zhang Jisen using a trick. In this circle of love, a new situation was created after the change. (To be continued)
